<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="193" data-file-width="193" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg/40px-Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg/60px-Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg/80px-Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikivoyage has a travel guide for <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikivoyage.org/wiki/North_Carolina#Q1454" title="wikivoyage:North Carolina">North Carolina</a></b></i>.</td>

<p><b>North Carolina</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">ɔːr</span><span title="/θ/: 'th' in 'thigh'">θ</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ær/: 'arr' in 'marry'">ær</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-North_Carolina.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/62/En-us-North_Carolina.ogg" title="En-us-North Carolina.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">southeastern region</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The state borders <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> to the north, and the Atlantic Ocean to the east. North Carolina is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">28th most extensive</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">9th most populous</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states" title="List of U.S. states">U.S. states</a>. The state is divided into <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_North_Carolina" title="List of counties in North Carolina">100 counties</a>. The capital is <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh</a>. The most populous municipality is <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a>, which is the third largest banking center in the United States after New York City and San Francisco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charlotte_Observer_2017-05-23_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Charlotte_Observer_2017-05-23-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state has a wide range of elevations, from sea level on the coast to 6,684 feet (2,037 m) at <a href="/wiki/Mount_Mitchell" title="Mount Mitchell">Mount Mitchell</a>, the highest point in North America east of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The climate of the coastal plains is strongly influenced by the Atlantic Ocean. Most of the state falls in the <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> zone. More than 300 miles (500 km) from the coast, the western, mountainous part of the state has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_highland_climate" title="Subtropical highland climate">subtropical highland climate</a>.</p>
<p></p>

</div>
</div>
<p>North Carolina is bordered by <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> on the south, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> on the southwest, <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> on the west, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> on the north, and the Atlantic Ocean on the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dpi_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-dpi-10">[10]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> places North Carolina in the <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_States" title="South Atlantic States">South Atlantic</a> division of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">southern</a> region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Carolina consists of three main geographic regions: the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_coastal_plain" title="Atlantic coastal plain">Atlantic coastal plain</a>, occupying the eastern portion of the state; the central <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_(United_States)" title="Piedmont (United States)">Piedmont</a> region, and the Mountain region in the west, which is part of the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dpi_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-dpi-10">[10]</a></sup> The coastal plain consists of more specifically-defined areas known as the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Banks" title="Outer Banks">Outer Banks</a>, a string of sandy, narrow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barrier_islands" title="Barrier islands">barrier islands</a> separated from the mainland by sounds or inlets, including <a href="/wiki/Albemarle_Sound" title="Albemarle Sound">Albemarle Sound</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pamlico_Sound" title="Pamlico Sound">Pamlico Sound</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidewater_(geographic_term)" title="Tidewater (geographic term)">tidewater</a> region, the native home of the <a href="/wiki/Venus_flytrap" title="Venus flytrap">venus flytrap</a>, and the inner coastal plain, where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Longleaf_pine" title="Longleaf pine">longleaf pine</a> trees are native.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dpi_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-dpi-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>So many ships have been lost off <a href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras" title="Cape Hatteras">Cape Hatteras</a> that the area is known as the "<a href="/wiki/Graveyard_of_the_Atlantic" title="Graveyard of the Atlantic">Graveyard of the Atlantic</a>";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dpi_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-dpi-10">[10]</a></sup> more than 1,000 ships have sunk in these waters since records began in 1526. The most famous of these is the <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne%27s_Revenge" title="Queen Anne's Revenge">Queen Anne's Revenge</a></i> (flagship of the pirate <a href="/wiki/Blackbeard" title="Blackbeard">Blackbeard</a>), which went aground in Beaufort Inlet in 1718.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The coastal plain transitions to the Piedmont region along the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Seaboard_fall_line" title="Atlantic Seaboard fall line">Atlantic Seaboard fall line</a>, the elevation at which waterfalls first appear on streams and rivers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dpi_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-dpi-10">[10]</a></sup> The Piedmont region of central North Carolina is the state's most populous region, containing the six largest cities in the state by population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> It consists of gently rolling countryside frequently broken by hills or low mountain ridges. Small, isolated, and deeply eroded mountain ranges and peaks are located in the Piedmont, including the <a href="/wiki/Sauratown_Mountains" title="Sauratown Mountains">Sauratown Mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pilot_Mountain_(North_Carolina)" title="Pilot Mountain (North Carolina)">Pilot Mountain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Uwharrie_Mountains" title="Uwharrie Mountains">Uwharrie Mountains</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crowder%27s_Mountain" title="Crowder's Mountain">Crowder's Mountain</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King%27s_Pinnacle" title="King's Pinnacle">King's Pinnacle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brushy_Mountains_(North_Carolina)" title="Brushy Mountains (North Carolina)">Brushy Mountains</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/South_Mountains_(North_Carolina)" title="South Mountains (North Carolina)">South Mountains</a>. The Piedmont ranges from about 300 feet (91 m) in elevation in the east to about 1,500 feet (460 m) in the west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dpi_10-5"><a href="#cite_note-dpi-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Western_North_Carolina" title="Western North Carolina">western section</a> of the state is part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountain" title="Appalachian Mountain">Appalachian Mountain</a> range. Among the subranges of the Appalachians located in the state are the <a href="/wiki/Great_Smoky_Mountains" title="Great Smoky Mountains">Great Smoky Mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Mountains" title="Blue Ridge Mountains">Blue Ridge Mountains</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Black_Mountains_(North_Carolina)" title="Black Mountains (North Carolina)">Black Mountains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-visitnc_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-visitnc-15">[15]</a></sup> The Black Mountains are the highest in the eastern United States, and culminate in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Mitchell_(North_Carolina)" title="Mount Mitchell (North Carolina)">Mount Mitchell</a> at 6,684 feet (2,037 m), the highest point east of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-visitnc_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-visitnc-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgs_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-usgs-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cullasaja.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="397" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Cullasaja.jpg/170px-Cullasaja.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Cullasaja.jpg/255px-Cullasaja.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Cullasaja.jpg/340px-Cullasaja.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cullasaja.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cullasaja_Falls" title="Cullasaja Falls">Cullasaja Falls</a> in <a href="/wiki/Macon_County,_North_Carolina" title="Macon County, North Carolina">Macon County</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>North Carolina has 17 major river basins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rivers_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-rivers-17">[17]</a></sup> The five basins west of the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Mountains" title="Blue Ridge Mountains">Blue Ridge Mountains</a> flow to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, while the remainder flow to the Atlantic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rivers_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-rivers-17">[17]</a></sup> Of the 17 basins, 11 originate within the state of North Carolina, but only four are contained entirely within the state's border – the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Fear_River" title="Cape Fear River">Cape Fear</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Neuse_River" title="Neuse River">Neuse</a>, the <a href="/wiki/White_Oak_River" title="White Oak River">White Oak</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Tar_River" title="Tar River">Tar</a>–<a href="/wiki/Pamlico_Sound" title="Pamlico Sound">Pamlico</a> basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_taxa_described_from_North_Carolina" title="List of taxa described from North Carolina">List of taxa described from North Carolina</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_North_Carolina" title="Climate of North Carolina">Climate of North Carolina</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Snow_in_old_fort.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Snow_in_old_fort.JPG/220px-Snow_in_old_fort.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Snow_in_old_fort.JPG/330px-Snow_in_old_fort.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Snow_in_old_fort.JPG/440px-Snow_in_old_fort.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Graveyard_Fields_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1998" data-file-width="3024" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Graveyard_Fields_3.jpg/220px-Graveyard_Fields_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Graveyard_Fields_3.jpg/330px-Graveyard_Fields_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Graveyard_Fields_3.jpg/440px-Graveyard_Fields_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2009_Coca-Cola_600.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/2009_Coca-Cola_600.jpg/220px-2009_Coca-Cola_600.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/2009_Coca-Cola_600.jpg/330px-2009_Coca-Cola_600.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/2009_Coca-Cola_600.jpg/440px-2009_Coca-Cola_600.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2009_Coca-Cola_600.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A rainy day at <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Motor_Speedway" title="Charlotte Motor Speedway">Charlotte Motor Speedway</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Elevation above sea level is most responsible for temperature change across the state, with the mountain area being coolest year-round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncclimate_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncclimate-19">[19]</a></sup> The climate is also influenced by the Atlantic Ocean and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>, especially in the coastal plain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncclimate_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-ncclimate-19">[19]</a></sup> These influences tend to cause warmer winter temperatures along the coast,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncclimate_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-ncclimate-19">[19]</a></sup> where temperatures only occasionally drop below the freezing point at night. The coastal plain averages around 1 inch (2.5 cm) of snow or ice annually, and in many years, there may be no snow or ice at all.</p>
<p>The Atlantic Ocean exerts less influence on the climate of the Piedmont region, which has hotter summers and colder winters than along the coast, though the average daily maximum is still below 90 °F (32 °C) in most locations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncclimate_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-ncclimate-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Carolina experiences severe weather in both summer and winter, with summer bringing threat of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" title="Tropical storm">hurricanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#tropical_storm" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical storms</a>, heavy rain, and flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Destructive hurricanes that have hit North Carolina include <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fran" title="Hurricane Fran">Hurricane Fran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Floyd" title="Hurricane Floyd">Hurricane Floyd</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hazel" title="Hurricane Hazel">Hurricane Hazel</a>, the latter being the strongest storm ever to make landfall in the state, as a <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Category 4</a> in 1954. <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Isabel" title="Hurricane Isabel">Hurricane Isabel</a> ranks as the most destructive of the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Carolina averages fewer than 20 tornadoes per year, many of them produced by hurricanes or tropical storms along the coastal plain. Tornadoes from thunderstorms are a risk, especially in the eastern part of the state. The western Piedmont is often protected by the mountains, which tend to break up storms as they try to cross over; the storms will often re-form farther east. A phenomenon known as "<a href="/wiki/Cold-air_damming" title="Cold-air damming">cold-air damming</a>" often occurs in the northwestern part of the state, which can weaken storms but can also lead to major ice events in winter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2011, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-April_2011_Southern_United_States_tornado_outbreak" title="Mid-April 2011 Southern United States tornado outbreak">the worst tornado outbreak</a> in North Carolina's history occurred. Thirty confirmed tornadoes touched down, mainly in the Eastern Piedmont and Sandhills, killing at least 24 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_Carolina" title="History of North Carolina">History of North Carolina</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:North-Carolina-Museum-of-History-20080321.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/North-Carolina-Museum-of-History-20080321.jpeg/220px-North-Carolina-Museum-of-History-20080321.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/North-Carolina-Museum-of-History-20080321.jpeg/330px-North-Carolina-Museum-of-History-20080321.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/North-Carolina-Museum-of-History-20080321.jpeg/440px-North-Carolina-Museum-of-History-20080321.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:North-Carolina-Museum-of-History-20080321.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Museum_of_History" title="North Carolina Museum of History">North Carolina Museum of History</a>, Raleigh</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Woodland-culture American Indians were in the area around 1000 BCE; starting around 750 CE, Mississippian-culture Indians created larger political units with stronger leadership and more stable, longer-term settlements. During this time, important buildings were constructed as pyramidal, flat-topped buildings. By 1550, many groups of American Indians lived in present-day North Carolina, including <a href="/wiki/Chowanoke" title="Chowanoke">Chowanoke</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roanoke_tribe" title="Roanoke tribe">Roanoke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pamlico" title="Pamlico">Pamlico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machapunga" title="Machapunga">Machapunga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coree" title="Coree">Coree</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Fear_Indians" title="Cape Fear Indians">Cape Fear Indians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waxhaw_tribe" title="Waxhaw tribe">Waxhaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waccamaw" title="Waccamaw">Waccamaw</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Catawba_people" title="Catawba people">Catawba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncmuseum_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncmuseum-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Juan_Pardo_(explorer)" title="Juan Pardo (explorer)">Juan Pardo</a> explored the area in 1566–1567, establishing <a href="/wiki/Fort_San_Juan_(Joara)" title="Fort San Juan (Joara)">Fort San Juan</a> in 1567 at the site of the Native American community of <a href="/wiki/Joara" title="Joara">Joara</a>, a Mississippian culture regional <a href="/wiki/Chiefdom" title="Chiefdom">chiefdom</a> in the western interior, near the present-day city of <a href="/wiki/Morganton,_North_Carolina" title="Morganton, North Carolina">Morganton</a>. The fort lasted only 18 months; the local inhabitants killed all but one of the 120 men Pardo had stationed at a total of six forts in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-richards_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-richards-33">[33]</a></sup> A later expedition by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Amadas" title="Philip Amadas">Philip Amadas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Barlowe" title="Arthur Barlowe">Arthur Barlowe</a> followed in 1584, at the direction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Walter_Raleigh" title="Sir Walter Raleigh">Sir Walter Raleigh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncmuseum_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-ncmuseum-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 1718, the pirate <a href="/wiki/Blackbeard" title="Blackbeard">Blackbeard</a> ran his flagship, the <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne%27s_Revenge" title="Queen Anne's Revenge">Queen Anne's Revenge</a></i>, aground at Beaufort Inlet, North Carolina, in present-day <a href="/wiki/Carteret_County,_North_Carolina" title="Carteret County, North Carolina">Carteret County</a>. After the grounding her crew and supplies were transferred to smaller ships. In November, after appealing to the governor of North Carolina, who promised safe-haven and a pardon, Blackbeard was killed in an ambush by troops from Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In 1996 Intersal, Inc., a private firm, discovered the remains of a vessel likely to be the <i>Queen Anne's Revenge</i>, which was added to the US <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-D._Moore._1997_pp._31_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-D._Moore._1997_pp._31-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Carolina became one of the English <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> and with the territory of <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> was originally known as the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Carolina" title="Province of Carolina">Province of Carolina</a>. The northern and southern parts of the original province separated in 1729. Originally settled by small farmers, sometimes having a few slaves, who were oriented toward subsistence agriculture, the colony lacked cities or towns. <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">Pirates</a> menaced the coastal settlements, but by 1718 the pirates had been captured and killed. Growth was strong in the middle of the 18th century, as the economy attracted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scotch-Irish_American" title="Scotch-Irish American">Scots-Irish</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quaker" title="Quaker">Quaker</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">German</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrants" title="Immigrants">immigrants</a>. The colonists generally supported the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, as the number of <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">Loyalists</a> was smaller than in some other colonies.</p>
<p>During colonial times, <a href="/wiki/Edenton,_North_Carolina" title="Edenton, North Carolina">Edenton</a> served as the state capital beginning in 1722, and <a href="/wiki/New_Bern,_North_Carolina" title="New Bern, North Carolina">New Bern</a> was selected as the capital in 1766. Construction of <a href="/wiki/Tryon_Palace" title="Tryon Palace">Tryon Palace</a>, which served as the residence and offices of the provincial governor <a href="/wiki/William_Tryon" title="William Tryon">William Tryon</a>, began in 1767 and was completed in 1771. In 1788 <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh</a> was chosen as the site of the new capital, as its central location protected it from coastal attacks. Officially established in 1792 as both county seat and state capital, the city was named after Sir <a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh">Walter Raleigh</a>, sponsor of <a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Colony" title="Roanoke Colony">Roanoke</a>, the "lost colony" on <a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Island" title="Roanoke Island">Roanoke Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Carolina made the smallest per-capita contribution to the war of any state, as only 7,800 men joined the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">Continental Army</a> under General <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>; an additional 10,000 served in local militia units under such leaders as General <a href="/wiki/Nathanael_Greene" title="Nathanael Greene">Nathanael Greene</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> There was some military action, especially in 1780–81. Many Carolinian frontiersmen had moved west over the mountains, into the <a href="/wiki/Washington_District,_North_Carolina" title="Washington District, North Carolina">Washington District</a> (later known as <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>), but in 1789, following the Revolution, the state was persuaded to relinquish its claim to the western lands. It ceded them to the national government so that the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territory" title="Northwest Territory">Northwest Territory</a> could be organized and managed nationally.</p>
<p>After 1800, cotton and <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a> became important export crops. The eastern half of the state, especially the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidewater_(geographic_term)" title="Tidewater (geographic term)">Tidewater</a> region, developed a slave society based on a <a href="/wiki/Plantations_in_the_American_South" title="Plantations in the American South">plantation</a> system and <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slave</a> labor. Many <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a> migrated to the frontier along with their European-American neighbors, where the social system was looser. By 1810, nearly 3 percent of the free population consisted of free people of color, who numbered slightly more than 10,000. The western areas were dominated by white families, especially Scots-Irish, who operated small subsistence farms. In the early national period, the state became a center of <a href="/wiki/Jeffersonian_democracy" title="Jeffersonian democracy">Jeffersonian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jacksonian_democracy" title="Jacksonian democracy">Jacksonian democracy</a>, with a strong <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">Whig</a> presence, especially in the West. After <a href="/wiki/Nat_Turner" title="Nat Turner">Nat Turner</a>'s slave uprising in 1831, North Carolina and other southern states reduced the rights of free blacks. In 1835 the legislature withdrew their right to vote.</p>
<p>On May 20, 1861, North Carolina was the last of the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate states</a> to declare <a href="/wiki/Secession" title="Secession">secession</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a>, 13 days after the Tennessee legislature voted for secession. Some 125,000 North Carolinians served in the military; 20,000 were killed in battle, the most of any state in the Confederacy, and 21,000 died of disease. The state government was reluctant to support the demands of the national government in <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond</a>, and the state was the scene of only small battles.</p>
<p>With the defeat of the Confederacy in 1865, the <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Era" title="Reconstruction Era">Reconstruction Era</a> began. The United States abolished slavery without compensation to slaveholders or reparations to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedmen" title="Freedmen">freedmen</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> coalition of black freedmen, northern <a href="/wiki/Carpetbagger" title="Carpetbagger">carpetbaggers</a> and local <a href="/wiki/Scalawag" title="Scalawag">scalawags</a> controlled state government for three years. The white conservative Democrats regained control of the state legislature in 1870, in part by <a href="/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan" title="Ku Klux Klan">Ku Klux Klan</a> violence and terrorism at the polls, to suppress black voting. Republicans were elected to the governorship until 1876, when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Shirts_(Southern_United_States)" title="Red Shirts (Southern United States)">Red Shirts</a>, a paramilitary organization that arose in 1874 and was allied with the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a>, helped suppress black voting. More than 150 black Americans were murdered in electoral violence in 1876.</p>
<p>Democrats were elected to the legislature and governor's office, but the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(United_States)" title="People's Party (United States)">Populists</a> attracted voters displeased with them. In 1896 a biracial, Populist-Republican Fusionist coalition gained the governor's office. The Democrats regained control of the legislature in 1896 and passed laws to impose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jim_Crow" title="Jim Crow">Jim Crow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">racial segregation</a> of public facilities. Voters of North Carolina's 2nd congressional district elected a total of four African-American <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">congressmen</a> through these years of the late 19th century.</p>
<p>Political tensions ran so high that a small group of white Democrats in 1898 planned to take over the <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_North_Carolina" title="Wilmington, North Carolina">Wilmington</a> government if their candidates were not elected. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilmington_Insurrection_of_1898" title="Wilmington Insurrection of 1898">Wilmington Insurrection of 1898</a>, more than 1,500 white men attacked the black newspaper and neighborhood, killed numerous men, and ran off the white Republican mayor and aldermen. They installed their own people and elected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfred_M._Waddell" title="Alfred M. Waddell">Alfred M. Waddell</a> as mayor, in the only <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> in United States history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Commission_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Commission-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1899 the state legislature passed a new constitution, with requirements for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tax_per_head" title="Tax per head">poll taxes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Literacy_test" title="Literacy test">literacy tests</a> for voter registration which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disfranchisement_after_the_Reconstruction_Era" title="Disfranchisement after the Reconstruction Era">disfranchised</a> most black Americans in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pildes_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pildes-39">[39]</a></sup> Exclusion from voting had wide effects: it meant that black Americans could not serve on juries or in any local office. After a decade of <a href="/wiki/White_supremacy" title="White supremacy">white supremacy</a>, many people forgot that North Carolina had ever had thriving middle-class black Americans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Black citizens had no political voice in the state until after the federal <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a> and <a href="/wiki/Voting_Rights_Act_of_1965" title="Voting Rights Act of 1965">Voting Rights Act of 1965</a> were passed to enforce their constitutional rights. It was not until 1992 that another <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a> was elected as a US Representative from North Carolina.</p>
<p>As in the rest of the former Confederacy, North Carolina had become a one-party state, dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a>. Impoverished by the Civil War, the state continued with an economy based on tobacco, cotton and agriculture. Towns and cities remained few in the east. A major industrial base emerged in the late 19th century in the western counties of the Piedmont, based on cotton mills established at the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Seaboard_fall_line" title="Atlantic Seaboard fall line">fall line</a>. Railroads were built to connect the new industrializing cities. The state was the site of the first successful controlled, powered and sustained heavier-than-air flight, by the <a href="/wiki/Wright_brothers" title="Wright brothers">Wright brothers</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Kitty_Hawk,_North_Carolina" title="Kitty Hawk, North Carolina">Kitty Hawk</a> on December 17, 1903. In the first half of the 20th century, many African Americans left the state to go North for better opportunities, in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">Great Migration</a>. Their departure changed the demographic characteristics of many areas.</p>
<p>North Carolina was hard hit by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression_in_the_United_States" title="Great Depression in the United States">Great Depression</a>, but the <a href="/wiki/New_Deal" title="New Deal">New Deal</a> programs of <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> for cotton and tobacco significantly helped the farmers. After World War II, the state's economy grew rapidly, highlighted by the growth of such cities as Charlotte, Raleigh, and Durham in the Piedmont. Raleigh, Durham, and Chapel Hill form the <a href="/wiki/Research_Triangle" title="Research Triangle">Research Triangle</a>, a major area of universities and advanced scientific and technical research. In the 1990s, Charlotte became a major regional and national banking center. Tourism has also been a boon for the North Carolina economy as people flock to the Outer Banks coastal area and the Appalachian Mountains anchored by Asheville.</p>
<p>By the 1970s, spurred in part by the increasingly leftward tilt of national Democrats, conservative whites began to vote for Republican national candidates and gradually for more Republicans locally. The <a href="/wiki/Greensboro_sit-ins" title="Greensboro sit-ins">Greensboro Sit-ins</a> played a crucial role in the Civil Rights Movement to bring full equality to American blacks.</p>
<h3><span id="Native_Americans,_lost_colonies,_and_permanent_settlement"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Native_Americans.2C_lost_colonies.2C_and_permanent_settlement">Native Americans, lost colonies, and permanent settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Native Americans, lost colonies, and permanent settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native Americans in the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joara" title="Joara">Joara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Island" title="Roanoke Island">Roanoke Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Raleigh_National_Historic_Site" title="Fort Raleigh National Historic Site">Fort Raleigh National Historic Site</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Carte_of_all_the_Coast_of_Virginia_by_Theodor_de_Bry_1585_1586.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="739" data-file-width="1000" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/The_Carte_of_all_the_Coast_of_Virginia_by_Theodor_de_Bry_1585_1586.jpg/220px-The_Carte_of_all_the_Coast_of_Virginia_by_Theodor_de_Bry_1585_1586.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/The_Carte_of_all_the_Coast_of_Virginia_by_Theodor_de_Bry_1585_1586.jpg/330px-The_Carte_of_all_the_Coast_of_Virginia_by_Theodor_de_Bry_1585_1586.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/The_Carte_of_all_the_Coast_of_Virginia_by_Theodor_de_Bry_1585_1586.jpg/440px-The_Carte_of_all_the_Coast_of_Virginia_by_Theodor_de_Bry_1585_1586.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Carte_of_all_the_Coast_of_Virginia_by_Theodor_de_Bry_1585_1586.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the coast of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> and North Carolina, drawn 1585–1586 by <a href="/wiki/Theodor_de_Bry" title="Theodor de Bry">Theodor de Bry</a>, based on map by <a href="/wiki/John_White_(colonist_and_artist)" title="John White (colonist and artist)">John White</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Colony" title="Roanoke Colony">Roanoke Colony</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>North Carolina was inhabited for thousands of years by succeeding cultures of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prehistoric" title="Prehistoric">prehistoric</a> <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> cultures. Before 200 AD, they were building <a href="/wiki/Earthworks_(archaeology)" title="Earthworks (archaeology)">earthwork mounds</a>, which were used for ceremonial and religious purposes. Succeeding peoples, including those of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_culture" title="Mississippian culture">Mississippian culture</a> established by 1000 AD in the Piedmont, continued to build or add on to such mounds. In the 500–700 years preceding European contact, the Mississippian culture built large, complex cities and maintained far-flung regional trading networks. Its largest city was <a href="/wiki/Cahokia" title="Cahokia">Cahokia</a>, located in present-day Illinois near the Mississippi River.</p>
<p>Historically documented tribes in the North Carolina region include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carolina_Algonquian" title="Carolina Algonquian">Carolina Algonquian</a>-speaking tribes of the coastal areas, such as the <a href="/wiki/Chowanoke" title="Chowanoke">Chowanoke</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roanoke_(tribe)" title="Roanoke (tribe)">Roanoke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pamlico" title="Pamlico">Pamlico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machapunga" title="Machapunga">Machapunga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coree" title="Coree">Coree</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Fear_Indians" title="Cape Fear Indians">Cape Fear Indians</a>, who were the first encountered by the English; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iroquoian" title="Iroquoian">Iroquoian</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Meherrin" title="Meherrin">Meherrin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cherokee" title="Cherokee">Cherokee</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuscarora_(tribe)" title="Tuscarora (tribe)">Tuscarora</a> of the interior; and Southeastern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siouan" title="Siouan">Siouan</a> tribes, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheraw_(tribe)" title="Cheraw (tribe)">Cheraw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waxhaws" title="Waxhaws">Waxhaw</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saponi" title="Saponi">Saponi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waccamaw_Siouan" title="Waccamaw Siouan">Waccamaw</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catawba_(tribe)" title="Catawba (tribe)">Catawba</a>.</p>
<p>Spanish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Explorer" title="Explorer">explorers</a> traveling inland in the 16th century met <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_culture" title="Mississippian culture">Mississippian culture</a> people at <a href="/wiki/Joara" title="Joara">Joara</a>, a regional <a href="/wiki/Chiefdom" title="Chiefdom">chiefdom</a> near present-day <a href="/wiki/Morganton,_North_Carolina" title="Morganton, North Carolina">Morganton</a>. Records of <a href="/wiki/Hernando_de_Soto" title="Hernando de Soto">Hernando de Soto</a> attested to his meeting with them in 1540. In 1567 Captain <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pardo_(explorer)" title="Juan Pardo (explorer)">Juan Pardo</a> led an expedition to claim the area for the Spanish colony and to establish another route to protect silver mines in Mexico. Pardo made a winter base at Joara, which he renamed <i>Cuenca</i>. His expedition built Fort San Juan and left a contingent of 30 men there, while Pardo traveled further, and built and garrisoned five other forts. He returned by a different route to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_Santa_Elena" title="Mission Santa Elena">Santa Elena</a> on <a href="/wiki/Parris_Island,_South_Carolina" title="Parris Island, South Carolina">Parris Island, South Carolina</a>, then a center of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a>. In the spring of 1568, natives killed all but one of the soldiers and burned the six forts in the interior, including the one at Fort San Juan. Although the Spanish never returned to the interior, this effort marked the first European attempt at colonization of the interior of what became the United States. A 16th-century journal by Pardo's scribe Bandera and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaeological" title="Archaeological">archaeological</a> findings since 1986 at Joara have confirmed the settlement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-richards_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-richards-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Croatoan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="263" data-file-width="418" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Croatoan.jpg/220px-Croatoan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Croatoan.jpg/330px-Croatoan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/81/Croatoan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Croatoan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/John_White_(colonist_and_artist)" title="John White (colonist and artist)">John White</a> returns to find the colony abandoned.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1584, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I" title="Elizabeth I">Elizabeth I</a> granted a charter to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Walter_Raleigh" title="Sir Walter Raleigh">Sir Walter Raleigh</a>, for whom the state capital is named, for land in present-day North Carolina (then part of the territory of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> It was the second American territory which the English attempted to colonize. Raleigh established two colonies on the coast in the late 1580s, but both failed. The fate of the "<a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Colony" title="Roanoke Colony">Lost Colony</a>" of <a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Island" title="Roanoke Island">Roanoke Island</a> remains one of the most widely debated mysteries of American history. <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Dare" title="Virginia Dare">Virginia Dare</a>, the first English child to be born in North America, was born on Roanoke Island on August 18, 1587; <a href="/wiki/Dare_County,_North_Carolina" title="Dare County, North Carolina">Dare County</a> is named for her.</p>
<p>As early as 1650, settlers from the Virginia colony moved into the area of <a href="/wiki/Albemarle_Sound" title="Albemarle Sound">Albemarle Sound</a>. By 1663, King <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II of England</a> granted a charter to start a new colony on the North American continent; it generally established North Carolina's borders. He named it <i>Carolina</i> in honor of his father <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> By 1665, a second charter was issued to attempt to resolve territorial questions. In 1710, owing to disputes over governance, the Carolina colony began to split into North Carolina and <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>. The latter became a crown colony in 1729.</p>
<p>In the 1700s, a series of <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> epidemics swept the South, causing high fatalities among the Native Americans, who had no <a href="/wiki/Immunity_(medical)" title="Immunity (medical)">immunity</a> to the new disease (it had become <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endemic" title="Endemic">endemic</a> in Europe).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> According to the historian Russell Thornton, "The 1738 epidemic was said to have killed one-half of the <a href="/wiki/Cherokee" title="Cherokee">Cherokee</a>, with other tribes of the area suffering equally."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period_and_Revolutionary_War">Colonial period and Revolutionary War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Colonial period and Revolutionary War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Carolina" title="Province of Carolina">Province of Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_North_Carolina" title="Province of North Carolina">Province of North Carolina</a>, and <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tryon_Palace.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Tryon_Palace.JPG/220px-Tryon_Palace.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Tryon_Palace.JPG/330px-Tryon_Palace.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Tryon_Palace.JPG/440px-Tryon_Palace.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tryon_Palace.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Reconstructed royal governor's mansion <a href="/wiki/Tryon_Palace" title="Tryon Palace">Tryon Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Bern,_North_Carolina" title="New Bern, North Carolina">New Bern</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the Spanish in the 16th century, the first permanent European settlers of North Carolina were English colonists who migrated south from <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>. The latter had grown rapidly and land was less available. <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Batts" title="Nathaniel Batts">Nathaniel Batts</a> was documented as one of the first of these Virginian migrants. He settled south of the <a href="/wiki/Chowan_River" title="Chowan River">Chowan River</a> and east of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Dismal_Swamp" title="Great Dismal Swamp">Great Dismal Swamp</a> in 1655.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> By 1663, this northeastern area of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Carolina" title="Province of Carolina">Province of Carolina</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/Albemarle_Settlements" title="Albemarle Settlements">Albemarle Settlements</a>, was undergoing full-scale English settlement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> During the same period, the English monarch <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a> gave the province to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lords_Proprietors" title="Lords Proprietors">Lords Proprietors</a>, a group of noblemen who had helped restore Charles to the throne in 1660. The new province of "Carolina" was named in honor and memory of King <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a> (Latin: <i>Carolus</i>). In 1712, North Carolina became a separate colony. Except for the <a href="/wiki/John_Carteret,_2nd_Earl_Granville" title="John Carteret, 2nd Earl Granville">Earl Granville</a> holdings, it became a royal colony seventeen years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-48">[48]</a></sup> A large revolt happened in the state in 1711 known as <a href="/wiki/Cary%27s_Rebellion" title="Cary's Rebellion">Cary's Rebellion</a>.</p>
<p>Differences in the settlement patterns of eastern and western North Carolina, or the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Lowcountry" title="South Carolina Lowcountry">Low Country</a> and uplands, affected the political, economic, and social life of the state from the 18th until the 20th century. The Tidewater in eastern North Carolina was settled chiefly by immigrants from rural England and the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Scottish Highlands</a>. The upcountry of western North Carolina was settled chiefly by <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_people" title="Ulster Scots people">Scots-Irish</a>, English, and <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a> Protestants, the so-called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cohee" title="Cohee">cohee</a>". Arriving during the mid- to late 18th century, the Scots-Irish from what is today Northern Ireland were the largest non-English immigrant group before the Revolution; English indentured servants were overwhelmingly the largest immigrant group before the Revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census.gov_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-census.gov-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census.gov_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-census.gov-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, the English and Highland Scots of eastern North Carolina tended to remain loyal to the British Crown, because of longstanding business and personal connections with Great Britain. The English, Welsh, Scots-Irish, and German settlers of western North Carolina tended to favor American independence from Britain.</p>
<p>Most of the English colonists had arrived as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" title="Indentured servant">indentured servants</a>, hiring themselves out as laborers for a fixed period to pay for their passage. In the early years the line between indentured servants and African <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave" title="Slave">slaves</a> or laborers was fluid. Some Africans were allowed to earn their freedom before slavery became a lifelong status. Most of the <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free colored</a> families formed in North Carolina before the Revolution were descended from unions or marriages between free white women and enslaved or free African or African-American men. Because the mothers were free, their children were born free. Many had migrated or were descendants of migrants from colonial Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> As the flow of indentured laborers to the colony decreased with improving economic conditions in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, planters imported more slaves, and the state's legal delineations between free and slave status tightened, effectively hardening the latter into a racial caste. The economy's growth and prosperity was based on slave labor, devoted first to the production of tobacco.</p>
<p>On April 12, 1776, the colony became the first to instruct its delegates to the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">Continental Congress</a> to vote for independence from the British Crown, through the <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Resolves" title="Halifax Resolves">Halifax Resolves</a> passed by the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Provincial_Congress" title="North Carolina Provincial Congress">North Carolina Provincial Congress</a>. The dates of both of these events are memorialized on the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_North_Carolina" title="Flag of North Carolina">state flag</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seal_of_North_Carolina" title="Seal of North Carolina">state seal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCSeal_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-NCSeal-54">[54]</a></sup> Throughout the Revolutionary War, fierce <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla warfare</a> erupted between bands of pro-independence and pro-British colonists. In some cases the war was also an excuse to settle private grudges and rivalries. A major American victory in the war took place at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King%27s_Mountain" title="King's Mountain">King's Mountain</a> along the North Carolina–South Carolina border; on October 7, 1780, a force of 1000 mountain men from western North Carolina (including what is today the state of <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Virginia" title="Southwest Virginia">southwest Virginia</a> overwhelmed a force of some 1000 British troops led by Major <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Ferguson" title="Patrick Ferguson">Patrick Ferguson</a>. Most of the soldiers fighting for the British side in this battle were Carolinians who had remained loyal to the Crown (they were called "Tories" or Loyalists). The American victory at Kings Mountain gave the advantage to colonists who favored American independence, and it prevented the British Army from recruiting new soldiers from the Tories.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Guiliford_Courthouse_15_March_1781.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1383" data-file-width="1929" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Battle_of_Guiliford_Courthouse_15_March_1781.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Guiliford_Courthouse_15_March_1781.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Battle_of_Guiliford_Courthouse_15_March_1781.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Guiliford_Courthouse_15_March_1781.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Battle_of_Guiliford_Courthouse_15_March_1781.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Guiliford_Courthouse_15_March_1781.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Guiliford_Courthouse_15_March_1781.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1st Maryland Regiment holding the line at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guilford" title="Battle of Guilford">Battle of Guilford</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The road to <a href="/wiki/Yorktown,_Virginia" title="Yorktown, Virginia">Yorktown</a> and America's independence from <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> led through North Carolina. As the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> moved north from victories in <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camden,_South_Carolina" title="Camden, South Carolina">Camden, South Carolina</a>, the Southern Division of the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">Continental Army</a> and local militia prepared to meet them. Following General <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Morgan" title="Daniel Morgan">Daniel Morgan</a>'s victory over the British Cavalry Commander <a href="/wiki/Banastre_Tarleton" title="Banastre Tarleton">Banastre Tarleton</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cowpens" title="Battle of Cowpens">Battle of Cowpens</a> on January 17, 1781, southern commander <a href="/wiki/Nathanael_Greene" title="Nathanael Greene">Nathanael Greene</a> led British Lord <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Cornwallis" title="Charles Cornwallis">Charles Cornwallis</a> across the heartland of North Carolina, and away from the latter's base of supply in Charleston, South Carolina. This campaign is known as "The Race to the Dan" or "The Race for the River."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cowan%27s_Ford" title="Battle of Cowan's Ford">Battle of Cowan's Ford</a>, Cornwallis met resistance along the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Catawba_River" title="Catawba River">Catawba River</a> at Cowan's Ford on February 1, 1781, in an attempt to engage General Morgan's forces during a tactical withdrawal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Morgan had moved to the northern part of the state to combine with General Greene's newly recruited forces. Generals Greene and Cornwallis finally met at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guilford_Courthouse" title="Battle of Guilford Courthouse">Battle of Guilford Courthouse</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">Greensboro</a> on March 15, 1781. Although the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">British</a> troops held the field at the end of the battle, their casualties at the hands of the numerically superior Continental Army were crippling. Following this "<a href="/wiki/Pyrrhic_victory" title="Pyrrhic victory">Pyrrhic victory</a>", Cornwallis chose to move to the Virginia coastline to get reinforcements, and to allow the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> to protect his battered army. This decision would result in Cornwallis' eventual defeat at <a href="/wiki/Yorktown,_Virginia" title="Yorktown, Virginia">Yorktown, Virginia</a>, later in 1781. The Patriots' victory there guaranteed American independence.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antebellum_period">Antebellum period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Antebellum period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 21, 1789, North Carolina became the twelfth state to ratify the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">Constitution</a>. In 1840, it completed the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_State_Capitol" title="North Carolina State Capitol">state capitol</a> building in Raleigh, still standing today. Most of North Carolina's slave owners and large <a href="/wiki/Plantations_in_the_American_South" title="Plantations in the American South">plantations</a> were located in the eastern portion of the state. Although North Carolina's plantation system was smaller and less cohesive than that of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, or <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>, significant numbers of planters were concentrated in the counties around the port cities of Wilmington and Edenton, as well as suburban planters around the cities of Raleigh, Charlotte, and <a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">Durham</a> in the Piedmont. Planters owning large estates wielded significant political and socio-economic power in antebellum North Carolina, which was a slave society. They placed their interests above those of the generally non-slave-holding "yeoman" farmers of western North Carolina. In mid-century, the state's rural and commercial areas were connected by the construction of a 129-mile (208 km) wooden plank road, known as a "farmer's railroad", from <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville,_North_Carolina" title="Fayetteville, North Carolina">Fayetteville</a> in the east to <a href="/wiki/Bethania,_North_Carolina" title="Bethania, North Carolina">Bethania</a> (northwest of <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem,_North_Carolina" title="Winston-Salem, North Carolina">Winston-Salem</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_North_Carolina_roads_and_railroads_1854.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1630" data-file-width="2384" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_North_Carolina_roads_and_railroads_1854.jpg/220px-Map_North_Carolina_roads_and_railroads_1854.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_North_Carolina_roads_and_railroads_1854.jpg/330px-Map_North_Carolina_roads_and_railroads_1854.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_North_Carolina_roads_and_railroads_1854.jpg/440px-Map_North_Carolina_roads_and_railroads_1854.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_North_Carolina_roads_and_railroads_1854.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Map" title="Map">Map</a> of the roads and railroads of North Carolina, 1854</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Besides slaves, there were a number of <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a> in the state. Most were descended from free African Americans who had migrated along with neighbors from <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> during the 18th century. The majority were the descendants of unions in the working classes between white women, indentured servants or free, and African men, indentured, slave or free.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">Revolution</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious_Society_of_Friends" title="Religious Society of Friends">Quakers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mennonite" title="Mennonite">Mennonites</a> worked to persuade slaveholders to free their slaves. Some were inspired by their efforts and the language of the Revolution to arrange for <a href="/wiki/Manumission" title="Manumission">manumission</a> of their slaves. The number of free people of color rose markedly in the first couple of decades after the Revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 25, 1836, construction began on the <a href="/wiki/Wilmington_and_Raleigh_Railroad" title="Wilmington and Raleigh Railroad">Wilmington and Raleigh Railroad</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> to connect the port city of <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_North_Carolina" title="Wilmington, North Carolina">Wilmington</a> with the state capital of <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh</a>. In 1849 the North Carolina Railroad was created by act of the legislature to extend that railroad west to <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">Greensboro</a>, <a href="/wiki/High_Point,_North_Carolina" title="High Point, North Carolina">High Point</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a>. During the Civil War, the Wilmington-to-Raleigh stretch of the railroad would be vital to the Confederate war effort; supplies shipped into Wilmington would be moved by rail through Raleigh to the Confederate capital of <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond, Virginia</a>.</p>
<p>During the antebellum period, North Carolina was an overwhelmingly rural state, even by Southern standards. In 1860 only one North Carolina town, the port city of <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_North_Carolina" title="Wilmington, North Carolina">Wilmington</a>, had a population of more than 10,000. <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh</a>, the state capital, had barely more than 5,000 residents.</p>
<p>While slaveholding was slightly less concentrated than in some Southern states, according to the 1860 census, more than 330,000 people, or 33% of the population of 992,622, were enslaved African Americans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-census-59">[59]</a></sup> They lived and worked chiefly on plantations in the eastern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidewater_(geographic_term)" title="Tidewater (geographic term)">Tidewater</a>. In addition, 30,463 <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">free people of color</a> lived in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-census-59">[59]</a></sup> They were also concentrated in the eastern coastal plain, especially at port cities such as Wilmington and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Bern" title="New Bern">New Bern</a>, where a variety of jobs were available. Free African Americans were allowed to vote until 1835, when the state revoked their suffrage in restrictions following the slave rebellion of 1831 led by <a href="/wiki/Nat_Turner" title="Nat Turner">Nat Turner</a>. Southern slave codes criminalized willful killing of a slave in most cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slaves_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-slaves-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Civil_War">American Civil War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: American Civil War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="North Carolina in the American Civil War">North Carolina in the American Civil War</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Fort_Fisher.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="445" data-file-width="640" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Battle_of_Fort_Fisher.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Fort_Fisher.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Battle_of_Fort_Fisher.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Fort_Fisher.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Battle_of_Fort_Fisher.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Fort_Fisher.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Fort_Fisher.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Union captures <a href="/wiki/Fort_Fisher" title="Fort Fisher">Fort Fisher</a>, 1865</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1860, North Carolina was a slave state, in which one-third of the population was enslaved. This was a smaller proportion than in many Southern states. The state did not vote to join the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederacy</a> until President <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> called on it to invade its sister state, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>, becoming the last or second-to-last state to officially join the Confederacy. The title of "last to join the Confederacy" has been disputed; although Tennessee's informal secession on May 7, 1861, preceded North Carolina's official secession on May 20,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> the Tennessee legislature did not formally vote to secede until June 8, 1861.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Carolina was the site of few battles, but it provided the Confederacy with at least 125,000 troops, which is far more than any other state did. Approximately 40,000 of those troops died: more than half of disease, the remainder from battlefield wounds and from starvation. North Carolina also supplied about 15,000 Union troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Elected in 1862, Governor <a href="/wiki/Zebulon_Baird_Vance" title="Zebulon Baird Vance">Zebulon Baird Vance</a> tried to maintain state autonomy against Confederate President <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Davis" title="Jefferson Davis">Jefferson Davis</a> in <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Virginia" title="Richmond, Virginia">Richmond</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Silent_Sam.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="655" data-file-width="622" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Silent_Sam.jpg/220px-Silent_Sam.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Silent_Sam.jpg/330px-Silent_Sam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Silent_Sam.jpg/440px-Silent_Sam.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Silent_Sam.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sculpture of <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate</a> soldier <a href="/wiki/Silent_Sam" title="Silent Sam">Silent Sam</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill" title="University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill">University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill</a>, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Wilson_(sculptor)" title="John Wilson (sculptor)">John Wilson</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After secession, some North Carolinians refused to support the Confederacy. Some of the yeoman farmers in the state's mountains and western Piedmont region remained neutral during the Civil War, while some covertly supported the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a> cause during the conflict. Approximately 2,000 North Carolinians from western North Carolina enlisted in the <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">Union Army</a> and fought for the North in the war. Two additional Union Army regiments were raised in the coastal areas of the state, which were occupied by Union forces in 1862 and 1863. Numerous slaves escaped to Union lines, where they became essentially free.</p>
<p>Confederate troops from all parts of North Carolina served in virtually all the major battles of the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Northern_Virginia" title="Army of Northern Virginia">Army of Northern Virginia</a>, the Confederacy's most famous army. The largest battle fought in North Carolina was at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bentonville" title="Battle of Bentonville">Bentonville</a>, which was a futile attempt by Confederate General <a href="/wiki/Joseph_E._Johnston" title="Joseph E. Johnston">Joseph Johnston</a> to slow Union General <a href="/wiki/William_Tecumseh_Sherman" title="William Tecumseh Sherman">William Tecumseh Sherman</a>'s advance through the Carolinas in the spring of 1865.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_48-3"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-48">[48]</a></sup> In April 1865, after losing the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Morrisville" title="Battle of Morrisville">Battle of Morrisville</a>, Johnston surrendered to Sherman at <a href="/wiki/Bennett_Place" title="Bennett Place">Bennett Place</a>, in what is today <a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">Durham</a>. North Carolina's port city of <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_North_Carolina" title="Wilmington, North Carolina">Wilmington</a> was the last Confederate port to fall to the Union, in February 1865, after the Union won the nearby <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Fort_Fisher" title="Second Battle of Fort Fisher">Second Battle of Fort Fisher</a>, its major defense downriver.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2008-08-16_Bennett_Place_historic_site.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/2008-08-16_Bennett_Place_historic_site.jpg/220px-2008-08-16_Bennett_Place_historic_site.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/2008-08-16_Bennett_Place_historic_site.jpg/330px-2008-08-16_Bennett_Place_historic_site.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/2008-08-16_Bennett_Place_historic_site.jpg/440px-2008-08-16_Bennett_Place_historic_site.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2008-08-16_Bennett_Place_historic_site.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bennett_Place" title="Bennett Place">Bennett Place</a> historic site in <a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">Durham</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first Confederate soldier to be killed in the Civil War was Private Henry Wyatt from North Carolina, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Big_Bethel" title="Battle of Big Bethel">Battle of Big Bethel</a> in June 1861. At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gettysburg" title="Battle of Gettysburg">Battle of Gettysburg</a> in July 1863, the 26th North Carolina Regiment participated in <a href="/wiki/Pickett%27s_Charge" title="Pickett's Charge">Pickett/Pettigrew's Charge</a> and advanced the farthest into the Northern lines of any Confederate regiment. During the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chickamauga" title="Battle of Chickamauga">Battle of Chickamauga</a>, the 58th North Carolina Regiment advanced farther than any other regiment on Snodgrass Hill to push back the remaining Union forces from the battlefield. At <a href="/wiki/Appomattox_Court_House_National_Historical_Park" title="Appomattox Court House National Historical Park">Appomattox Court House</a> in Virginia in April 1865, the 75th North Carolina Regiment, a cavalry unit, fired the last shots of the Confederate <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Northern_Virginia" title="Army of Northern Virginia">Army of Northern Virginia</a> in the Civil War. For many years, North Carolinians proudly boasted that they had been "First at Bethel, Farthest at Gettysburg and Chickamauga, and Last at Appomattox."</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
