<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of North Carolina was 10,146,788 on July 1, 2016, a 6.4% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopHousingEst_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-PopHousingEst-4">[4]</a></sup> Of the people residing in North Carolina, 58.5% were born in North Carolina, 33.1% were born in another US state, 1.0% were born in Puerto Rico, U.S. Island areas, or born abroad to American parent(s), and 7.4% were born in another country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> As of 2011, 49.8% of North Carolina's population younger than age 1 were minorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Demographics of North Carolina</b> covers the varieties of ethnic groups that reside in North Carolina, along with the relevant trends.</p>
<p>The state's racial composition in the 2010 Census:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>

<p>As of 2011, 49.8% of North Carolina's population younger than age 1 were minorities (meaning that they had at least one parent who was not non-Hispanic white).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2010, 89.66% (7,750,904) of North Carolina residents age 5 and older spoke English at home as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_language" title="Primary language">primary language</a>, while 6.93% (598,756) spoke Spanish, 0.32% (27,310) French, 0.27% (23,204) German, and Chinese (which includes <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">Mandarin</a>) was spoken as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Main_language" title="Main language">main language</a> by 0.27% (23,072) of the population over the age of five. In total, 10.34% (893,735) of North Carolina's population age 5 and older spoke a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_language" title="Mother language">mother language</a> other than English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA_Data_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-MLA_Data-73">[73]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin-left:15px; margin-top:0;">
<tr>
<td colspan="3" style="background:#ccf; text-align:center;"><b>Religious affiliation</b></td>

</td>

</table>
<p>North Carolina residents, like those of other <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern</a> states, since the colonial era have historically been overwhelmingly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>, first Anglican, then Baptist and Methodist. By the late 19th century, the largest Protestant denomination was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist" title="Baptist">Baptist</a>. After the Civil War, black Baptists were not allowed in white churches, due to segregation, and set up their own independent congregations. Black Baptists went on to develop their own state and national associations, to be free of white supervision.</p>
<p>While the Baptists in total (counting both blacks and whites) have maintained the majority in this part of the country (known as the <a href="/wiki/Bible_Belt" title="Bible Belt">Bible Belt</a>), the population in North Carolina practices a wide variety of faiths, including <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baha%27i" title="Baha'i">Baha'i</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>. As of 2010 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Church" title="Southern Baptist Church">Southern Baptist Church</a> was the biggest denomination, with 4,241 churches and 1,513,000 members; the second largest was the United Methodist Church, with 660,000 members and 1,923 churches. The third was the Roman Catholic Church, with 428,000 members in 190 congregations. The fourth greatest was the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_(USA)" title="Presbyterian Church (USA)">Presbyterian Church (USA)</a>, with 186,000 members and 710 congregations; this denomination was brought by Scots-Irish immigrants who settled the backcountry in the colonial era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state also has a special history with the <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">Moravian Church</a>, as settlers of this faith (largely of German origin) found a home in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winston-Salem" title="Winston-Salem">Winston-Salem</a> area in the 18th and 19th centuries. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presbyterians" title="Presbyterians">Presbyterians</a>, historically Scots-Irish, have had a strong presence in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charlotte" title="Charlotte">Charlotte</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Scotland_County,_North_Carolina" title="Scotland County, North Carolina">Scotland County</a>.</p>
<p>Currently, the rapid influx of <a href="/wiki/Northern_United_States" title="Northern United States">northerners</a> and immigrants from Latin America is steadily increasing ethnic and religious diversity: the number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jews</a> in the state has increased, as well as general religious diversity. The second-largest Protestant denomination in North Carolina after Baptist traditions is <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodism</a>, which is strong in the northern Piedmont, especially in populous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guilford_County" title="Guilford County">Guilford County</a>. There are also a substantial number of <a href="/wiki/Quakers" title="Quakers">Quakers</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guilford_County" title="Guilford County">Guilford County</a> and northeastern North Carolina. Many universities and colleges in the state have been founded on religious traditions, and some currently maintain that affiliation, including:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Belmont_Abbey_College" title="Belmont Abbey College">Belmont Abbey College</a> (Catholic)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bennett_College_for_Women" title="Bennett College for Women">Bennett College for Women</a> (United Methodist Church)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Campbell_University" title="Campbell University">Campbell University</a> (Baptist)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Catawba_College" title="Catawba College">Catawba College</a> (United Church of Christ)</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Davidson_College" title="Davidson College">Davidson College</a> (Presbyterian)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke University</a> (Historically Methodist)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elon_University" title="Elon University">Elon University</a> (United Church of Christ)</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/High_Point_University" title="High Point University">High Point University</a> (United Methodist Church)</li>

<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenoir-Rhyne_University" title="Lenoir-Rhyne University">Lenoir-Rhyne University</a> (Evangelical Lutheran Church in America)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Livingstone_College" title="Livingstone College">Livingstone College</a> (African Methodist Episcopal Zion Church)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Louisburg_College" title="Louisburg College">Louisburg College</a> (United Methodist Church)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mars_Hill_University" title="Mars Hill University">Mars Hill University</a> (Christian)</li>

</ul>
</div>
<p>The state also has several major seminaries, including the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Baptist_Theological_Seminary" title="Southeastern Baptist Theological Seminary">Southeastern Baptist Theological Seminary</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wake_Forest,_North_Carolina" title="Wake Forest, North Carolina">Wake Forest</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hood_Theological_Seminary" title="Hood Theological Seminary">Hood Theological Seminary</a> (AME Zion) in <a href="/wiki/Salisbury" title="Salisbury">Salisbury</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Most_populated_counties">Most populated counties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Most populated counties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_North_Carolina" title="List of counties in North Carolina">List of counties in North Carolina</a></div>
<p>In 2016, the US Census Bureau released 2015 population estimate counts for North Carolina's counties. <a href="/wiki/Mecklenburg_County,_North_Carolina" title="Mecklenburg County, North Carolina">Mecklenburg County</a> has the largest population, while <a href="/wiki/Wake_County,_North_Carolina" title="Wake County, North Carolina">Wake County</a> has the second largest population in North Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_cities">Major cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Major cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_North_Carolina" title="List of municipalities in North Carolina">List of municipalities in North Carolina</a></div>
<p>In 2016, the US Census Bureau released 2015 population estimate counts for North Carolina's cities with populations above 70,000. <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a> has the largest population, while <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh</a> has the highest population density of North Carolina's largest cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_combined_statistical_areas">Largest combined statistical areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Largest combined statistical areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charlotte_Skyline_2011_-_Ricky_W.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="573" data-file-width="937" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Charlotte_Skyline_2011_-_Ricky_W.jpg/220px-Charlotte_Skyline_2011_-_Ricky_W.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Charlotte_Skyline_2011_-_Ricky_W.jpg/330px-Charlotte_Skyline_2011_-_Ricky_W.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Charlotte_Skyline_2011_-_Ricky_W.jpg/440px-Charlotte_Skyline_2011_-_Ricky_W.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charlotte_Skyline_2011_-_Ricky_W.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a> skyline</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>North Carolina has three major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_Statistical_Areas" title="Combined Statistical Areas">Combined Statistical Areas</a> with populations of more than 1.6 million (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">U.S. Census Bureau</a> 2015 estimates):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S._Census_Bureau_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._Census_Bureau-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Charlotte_metropolitan_area" title="Charlotte metropolitan area">Metrolina</a></b>: <i>Charlotte–Gastonia–Salisbury, North Carolina-South Carolina</i> – population 2,583,956<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S._Census_Bureau_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._Census_Bureau-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>The <a href="/wiki/Research_Triangle" title="Research Triangle">Research Triangle</a></b>: <i>Raleigh–Durham–Chapel Hill, North Carolina</i> – population 2,117,103<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S._Census_Bureau_82-2"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._Census_Bureau-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>The <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_Triad" title="Piedmont Triad">Piedmont Triad</a></b>: <i>Greensboro–Winston-Salem–High Point, North Carolina</i> – population 1,642,506<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-U.S._Census_Bureau_82-3"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._Census_Bureau-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_North_Carolina" title="Economy of North Carolina">Economy of North Carolina</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Carolina_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="North Carolina locations by per capita income">North Carolina locations by per capita income</a></div>
<p>North Carolina has a very diverse economy because of its great availability of hydroelectric power,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> its pleasant climate, and its wide variety of soils. The state ranks third among the South Atlantic states in population, but leads the region in industry<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and agriculture.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> North Carolina leads the nation in the production of tobacco<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, textiles<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, and furniture<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. Charlotte, the state's largest city, is a major textile and trade center. According to a Forbes article written in 2013 Employment in the "Old North State" has gained many different industry sectors. See the following article summary: science, technology, energy and math, or STEM, industries in the area surrounding North Carolina's capital have grown 17.9 percent since 2001, placing Raleigh-Cary at No. 5 among the 51 largest metro areas in the country where technology is booming. In 2010 North Carolina's total gross state product was $424.9 billion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stategdp_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-stategdp-83">[83]</a></sup> while the state debt in November 2012, according to one source, totalled US$2.4bn,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> while according to another, was in 2012 US$57.8bn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> In 2011 the civilian labor force was at around 4.5 million with employment near 4.1 million. The working population is employed across the major employment sectors. The <b>economy of North Carolina</b> covers 15 metropolitan areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glance_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-glance-86">[86]</a></sup> In 2010, North Carolina was chosen as the third-best state for business by Forbes Magazine, and the second-best state by Chief Executive Officer Magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Carolina is the leading US state in production of <a href="/wiki/Flue-cured_tobacco" title="Flue-cured tobacco">flue-cured tobacco</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet_potatoes" title="Sweet potatoes">sweet potatoes</a>, and is second in production of pigs and hogs, <a href="/wiki/Trout" title="Trout">trout</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkeys" title="Turkeys">turkeys</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncgov_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncgov-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lib_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-lib-89">[89]</a></sup> In the three most recent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USDA" title="USDA">USDA</a> surveys (2002, 2007, 2012), North Carolina also ranked second in <a href="/wiki/Christmas_tree" title="Christmas tree">Christmas tree</a> production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncgov_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-ncgov-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>Based on American Community Survey 2010-2014 data, North Carolina's median household income was $46,693. It ranked forty first out of fifty states plus the District of Columbia for median household income. North Carolina had the fourteenth highest poverty rate in the nation at 17.6%. 13% of families were below the poverty line. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2000, there has been a clear division in the economic growth of North Carolina's urban and rural areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-93">[93]</a></sup> While North Carolina's urban areas have enjoyed a prosperous economy with steady job growth, low unemployment, and rising wages,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-93">[93]</a></sup> many of the state's rural counties have suffered from job loss, rising levels of poverty, and population loss as their manufacturing base has declined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_93-2"><a href="#cite_note-auto-93">[93]</a></sup> According to one estimate, one-half of North Carolina's 100 counties have lost population since 2010, primarily due to the poor economy in many of North Carolina's rural areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_93-3"><a href="#cite_note-auto-93">[93]</a></sup> However, the population of the state's urban areas is steadily increasing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_93-4"><a href="#cite_note-auto-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_North_Carolina" title="Transportation in North Carolina">Transportation in North Carolina</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Balloonduck.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1414" data-file-width="1895" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Balloonduck.png/220px-Balloonduck.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Balloonduck.png/330px-Balloonduck.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Balloonduck.png/440px-Balloonduck.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Balloonduck.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A North Carolina license plate.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Transportation systems in North Carolina consist of air, water, road, rail, and public transportation including intercity rail via Amtrak and light rail in Charlotte. North Carolina has the second-largest state highway system in the country as well as the largest ferry system on the east coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Carolina's airports serve destinations throughout the United States and international destinations in Canada, Europe, Central America, and the Caribbean. In 2013 <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Douglas_International_Airport" title="Charlotte Douglas International Airport">Charlotte Douglas International Airport</a> ranked as the 23rd busiest airport in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Carolina has a growing passenger rail system with Amtrak serving most major cities. Charlotte is also home to North Carolina's only light rail system known as the Lynx.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_North_Carolina" title="Government of North Carolina">Government of North Carolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_North_Carolina" title="Politics of North Carolina">Politics of North Carolina</a></div>

<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>

<p>The government of North Carolina is divided into three branches: executive, legislative, and judicial. These consist of the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Council_of_State" title="North Carolina Council of State">Council of State</a> (led by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_North_Carolina" title="Governor of North Carolina">Governor</a>), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> legislature (called the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_General_Assembly" title="North Carolina General Assembly">General Assembly</a>), and the state court system (headed by the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Supreme_Court" title="North Carolina Supreme Court">North Carolina Supreme Court</a>). The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Constitution" title="North Carolina Constitution">state constitution</a> delineates the structure and function of the state government. North Carolina has 13 seats in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._House_of_Representatives" title="U.S. House of Representatives">U.S. House of Representatives</a> and two seats in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Senate" title="U.S. Senate">U.S. Senate</a>.</p>
<p>North Carolina's party loyalties have undergone a series of important shifts in the last few years: While the 2010 midterms saw Tar Heel voters elect a bicameral <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Republican_Party" title="North Carolina Republican Party">Republican</a> majority legislature for the first time in over a century, North Carolina has also become a Southern <a href="/wiki/Swing_state" title="Swing state">swing state</a> in presidential races. Since Southern Democrat <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>'s comfortable victory in the state in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_North_Carolina,_1976" title="United States presidential election in North Carolina, 1976">1976</a>, the state had consistently leaned Republican in presidential elections until Democrat <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> narrowly won the state in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_North_Carolina,_2008" title="United States presidential election in North Carolina, 2008">2008</a>. In the 1990s, Democrat <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> came within a point of winning the state in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_North_Carolina,_1992" title="United States presidential election in North Carolina, 1992">1992</a> and also only narrowly lost the state in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_North_Carolina,_1996" title="United States presidential election in North Carolina, 1996">1996</a>. In the early 2000s, Republican <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> easily won the state by over 12 points, but by 2008, demographic shifts, population growth, and increased liberalization in heavily populated areas such as the <a href="/wiki/Research_Triangle" title="Research Triangle">Research Triangle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">Greensboro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem,_North_Carolina" title="Winston-Salem, North Carolina">Winston-Salem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville,_North_Carolina" title="Fayetteville, North Carolina">Fayetteville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Asheville,_North_Carolina" title="Asheville, North Carolina">Asheville</a>, propelled Barack Obama to victory in North Carolina, the first Democrat to win the state since 1976. In <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_North_Carolina,_2012" title="United States presidential election in North Carolina, 2012">2012</a>, North Carolina was again considered a competitive swing state, with the Democrats even holding their <a href="/wiki/2012_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2012 Democratic National Convention">2012 Democratic National Convention</a> in Charlotte. However, Republican <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">Mitt Romney</a> ultimately eked out a 2-point win in North Carolina, the only 2012 swing state that Obama lost, and one of only two states (along with <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Indiana,_2012" title="United States presidential election in Indiana, 2012">Indiana</a>) to flip from Obama in 2008 to the GOP in 2012.</p>
<p>In 2012, the state elected a Republican Governor (<a href="/wiki/Pat_McCrory" title="Pat McCrory">Pat McCrory</a>) and Lieutenant Governor (<a href="/wiki/Dan_Forest" title="Dan Forest">Dan Forest</a>) for the first time in more than two decades, while also giving the Republicans veto-proof majorities in both the State House of Representatives and the State Senate. Several U.S. House of Representatives seats also flipped control, with the Republicans holding nine seats to the Democrats' four. In the 2014 mid-term elections, Republican <a href="/wiki/David_Rouzer" title="David Rouzer">David Rouzer</a> won the state's Seventh Congressional District seat, increasing the congressional delegation party split to 10-3 in favor of the GOP.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_education">Primary and secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kituwah_Academy.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A lesson at Kituwah Academy on the <a href="/wiki/Qualla_Boundary" title="Qualla Boundary">Qualla Boundary</a> in North Carolina. The <a href="/wiki/Language_immersion" title="Language immersion">language immersion</a> school, operated by the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Band_of_Cherokee_Indians" title="Eastern Band of Cherokee Indians">Eastern Band of Cherokee Indians</a>, teaches the same curriculum as other state <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_schools" title="Primary schools">primary schools</a>, but the <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> <a href="/wiki/Cherokee_language" title="Cherokee language">Cherokee language</a> is the medium of instruction from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-school" title="Pre-school">pre-school</a> on up and students learn it as a <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">first language</a>. Such schools have proven instrumental in the preservation and perpetuation of the Cherokee language.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Elementary and secondary public schools are overseen by the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Department_of_Public_Instruction" title="North Carolina Department of Public Instruction">North Carolina Department of Public Instruction</a>. The <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Superintendent_of_Public_Instruction" title="North Carolina Superintendent of Public Instruction">North Carolina Superintendent of Public Instruction</a> is the secretary of the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_State_Board_of_Education" title="North Carolina State Board of Education">North Carolina State Board of Education</a>, but the board, rather than the superintendent, holds most of the legal authority for making public education policy. In 2009, the board's chairman also became the "chief executive officer" for the state's school system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> North Carolina has 115 public school systems,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SchoolQF_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-SchoolQF-121">[121]</a></sup> each of which is overseen by a local school board. A county may have one or more systems within it. The largest school systems in North Carolina are the <a href="/wiki/Wake_County_Public_School_System" title="Wake County Public School System">Wake County Public School System</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlotte-Mecklenburg_Schools" title="Charlotte-Mecklenburg Schools">Charlotte-Mecklenburg Schools</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guilford_County_Schools" title="Guilford County Schools">Guilford County Schools</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem/Forsyth_County_Schools" title="Winston-Salem/Forsyth County Schools">Winston-Salem/Forsyth County Schools</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_County_Schools" title="Cumberland County Schools">Cumberland County Schools</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In total there are 2,425 public schools in the state, including 99 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charter_school_(North_Carolina)" title="Charter school (North Carolina)">charter schools</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SchoolQF_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-SchoolQF-121">[121]</a></sup> North Carolina Schools were segregated until the <a href="/wiki/Brown_v._Board_of_Education" title="Brown v. Board of Education">Brown v. Board of Education</a> trial and the release of the <a href="/wiki/Pearsall_Plan" title="Pearsall Plan">Pearsall Plan</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_North_Carolina" title="List of colleges and universities in North Carolina">List of colleges and universities in North Carolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_North_Carolina_by_enrollment" title="List of universities in North Carolina by enrollment">List of universities in North Carolina by enrollment</a></div>
<p>In 1795, North Carolina opened the first public university in the United States—the University of North Carolina (now named the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill" title="University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill">University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill</a>). More than 200 years later, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_system" title="University of North Carolina system">University of North Carolina system</a> encompasses 17 <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public universities</a> including <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_State_University" title="North Carolina State University">North Carolina State University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Carolina_A%26T_State_University" title="North Carolina A&amp;T State University">North Carolina A&amp;T State University</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Central_University" title="North Carolina Central University">North Carolina Central University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill" title="University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill">University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Greensboro" title="University of North Carolina at Greensboro">University of North Carolina at Greensboro</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Carolina_University" title="East Carolina University">East Carolina University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Carolina_University" title="Western Carolina University">Western Carolina University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem_State_University" title="Winston-Salem State University">Winston-Salem State University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Asheville" title="University of North Carolina at Asheville">University of North Carolina at Asheville</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Charlotte" title="University of North Carolina at Charlotte">University of North Carolina at Charlotte</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Pembroke" title="University of North Carolina at Pembroke">University of North Carolina at Pembroke</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNC_Wilmington" title="UNC Wilmington">UNC Wilmington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_City_State_University" title="Elizabeth City State University">Elizabeth City State University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_State_University" title="Appalachian State University">Appalachian State University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville_State_University" title="Fayetteville State University">Fayetteville State University</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNC_School_of_the_Arts" title="UNC School of the Arts">UNC School of the Arts</a>, and .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Along with its public universities, North Carolina has 58 public <a href="/wiki/Community_college" title="Community college">community colleges</a> in its <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Community_College_System" title="North Carolina Community College System">community college system</a>.The largest university in North Carolina is currently <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_State_University" title="North Carolina State University">North Carolina State University</a>, with more than 34,000 students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>

<p>North Carolina is also home to many well-known private colleges and universities, including <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wake_Forest_University" title="Wake Forest University">Wake Forest University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pfeiffer_University" title="Pfeiffer University">Pfeiffer University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lees-McRae_College" title="Lees-McRae College">Lees-McRae College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Davidson_College" title="Davidson College">Davidson College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barton_College" title="Barton College">Barton College</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Wesleyan_College" title="North Carolina Wesleyan College">North Carolina Wesleyan College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elon_University" title="Elon University">Elon University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guilford_College" title="Guilford College">Guilford College</a>, Livingstone College, <a href="/wiki/Salem_College" title="Salem College">Salem College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaw_University" title="Shaw University">Shaw University</a> (the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HBCU" title="HBCU">historically black college or university</a> in the South), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laurel_University" title="Laurel University">Laurel University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meredith_College" title="Meredith College">Meredith College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Methodist_University" title="Methodist University">Methodist University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belmont_Abbey_College" title="Belmont Abbey College">Belmont Abbey College</a> (the only Catholic college in the Carolinas), <a href="/wiki/Campbell_University" title="Campbell University">Campbell University</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mount_Olive" title="University of Mount Olive">University of Mount Olive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montreat_College" title="Montreat College">Montreat College</a>, <a href="/wiki/High_Point_University" title="High Point University">High Point University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenoir-Rhyne_University" title="Lenoir-Rhyne University">Lenoir-Rhyne University</a> (the only Lutheran university in North Carolina) and <a href="/wiki/Wingate_University" title="Wingate University">Wingate University</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_North_Carolina" title="Sports in North Carolina">Sports in North Carolina</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(August 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>North Carolina is home to three <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">major league</a> sports franchises: the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Hornets" title="Charlotte Hornets">Charlotte Hornets</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> are based in Charlotte, while the Raleigh-based <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Hurricanes" title="Carolina Hurricanes">Carolina Hurricanes</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>. The Panthers and Hurricanes are the only two major professional sports teams that have the same geographical designation while playing in different metropolitan areas. The Hurricanes are the only major professional team from North Carolina to have won a league championship, <a href="/wiki/2006_Stanley_Cup_Finals" title="2006 Stanley Cup Finals">having captured the Stanley Cup in 2006.</a> North Carolina is also home to two other top-level professional teams in less prominent sports—the Charlotte Hounds of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Lacrosse" title="Major League Lacrosse">Major League Lacrosse</a> and the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Courage" title="North Carolina Courage">North Carolina Courage</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Women%27s_Soccer_League" title="National Women's Soccer League">National Women's Soccer League</a>.</p>
<p>While North Carolina has no <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> team, it does have numerous minor league baseball teams, with the highest level of play coming from the <a href="/wiki/Triple-A_(baseball)" title="Triple-A (baseball)">AAA</a>-affiliated <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Knights" title="Charlotte Knights">Charlotte Knights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Durham_Bulls" title="Durham Bulls">Durham Bulls</a>. Additionally, North Carolina has minor league teams in other team sports including <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, most notably <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_FC" title="North Carolina FC">North Carolina FC</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Checkers" title="Charlotte Checkers">Charlotte Checkers</a>, both of which play in the second tier of their respective sports.</p>
<p>In addition to professional team sports, North Carolina has a strong affiliation with <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> and stock-car racing, with <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Motor_Speedway" title="Charlotte Motor Speedway">Charlotte Motor Speedway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Concord,_North_Carolina" title="Concord, North Carolina">Concord</a> hosting two <a href="/wiki/Monster_Energy_NASCAR_Cup_Series" title="Monster Energy NASCAR Cup Series">Cup Series</a> races every year. Charlotte also hosts the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Hall_of_Fame" title="NASCAR Hall of Fame">NASCAR Hall of Fame</a>, while Concord is the home of several top-flight racing teams, including <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_Motorsports" title="Hendrick Motorsports">Hendrick Motorsports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roush_Fenway_Racing" title="Roush Fenway Racing">Roush Fenway Racing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Petty_Motorsports" title="Richard Petty Motorsports">Richard Petty Motorsports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stewart-Haas_Racing" title="Stewart-Haas Racing">Stewart-Haas Racing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chip_Ganassi_Racing" title="Chip Ganassi Racing">Chip Ganassi Racing</a>. Numerous other tracks around North Carolina host races from low-tier NASCAR circuits as well.</p>
<p>Golf is a popular summertime leisure activity, and North Carolina has hosted several important professional golf tournaments. <a href="/wiki/Pinehurst_Resort" title="Pinehurst Resort">Pinehurst Resort</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pinehurst,_North_Carolina" title="Pinehurst, North Carolina">Pinehurst</a> has hosted a <a href="/wiki/PGA_Championship" title="PGA Championship">PGA Championship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryder_Cup" title="Ryder Cup">Ryder Cup</a>, two <a href="/wiki/U.S._Open_(golf)" title="U.S. Open (golf)">U.S. Opens</a>, and one <a href="/wiki/United_States_Women%27s_Open_Championship_(golf)" title="United States Women's Open Championship (golf)">U.S. Women's Open</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Championship" title="Wells Fargo Championship">Wells Fargo Championship</a> is a regular stop on the <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour" title="PGA Tour">PGA Tour</a> and is held at <a href="/wiki/Quail_Hollow_Club" title="Quail Hollow Club">Quail Hollow Club</a> in Charlotte, while the <a href="/wiki/Wyndham_Championship" title="Wyndham Championship">Wyndham Championship</a> is played annually in Greensboro.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/College_athletics_in_the_United_States" title="College athletics in the United States">College sports</a> are also popular in North Carolina, with 18 schools competing at the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">Division I</a> level. The <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> (ACC) is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">Greensboro</a>, and both the <a href="/wiki/ACC_Championship_Game" title="ACC Championship Game">ACC Football Championship Game</a> (Charlotte) and the <a href="/wiki/ACC_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="ACC Men's Basketball Tournament">ACC Men's Basketball Tournament</a> (Greensboro) were most recently held in North Carolina. <a href="/wiki/College_basketball" title="College basketball">College basketball</a> in particular is very popular, buoyed by the <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_Road" title="Tobacco Road">Tobacco Road</a> rivalries between <a href="/wiki/Duke_Blue_Devils_men%27s_basketball" title="Duke Blue Devils men's basketball">Duke</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball" title="North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball">North Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/NC_State_Wolfpack_men%27s_basketball" title="NC State Wolfpack men's basketball">North Carolina State</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wake_Forest_Demon_Deacons_men%27s_basketball" title="Wake Forest Demon Deacons men's basketball">Wake Forest</a>. The <a href="/wiki/ACC_Championship_Game" title="ACC Championship Game">ACC Championship Game</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Belk_Bowl" title="Belk Bowl">Belk Bowl</a> are held annually in Charlotte's <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Stadium" title="Bank of America Stadium">Bank of America Stadium</a>, featuring teams from the ACC and the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a>. Additionally, the state has hosted the NCAA Men's Basketball <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Final_Four_(college_basketball)" title="Final Four (college basketball)">Final Four</a> on two occasions, in Greensboro in 1974 and in Charlotte in 1994.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(August 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biltmore_Estate_14.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1626" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Biltmore_Estate_14.jpg/220px-Biltmore_Estate_14.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Biltmore_Estate_14.jpg/330px-Biltmore_Estate_14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Biltmore_Estate_14.jpg/440px-Biltmore_Estate_14.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biltmore_Estate_14.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Biltmore_Estate" title="Biltmore Estate">Biltmore Estate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asheville,_North_Carolina" title="Asheville, North Carolina">Asheville</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Every year the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a> attract several million tourists to the Western part of the state, including the historic <a href="/wiki/Biltmore_Estate" title="Biltmore Estate">Biltmore Estate</a>. The scenic <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Parkway" title="Blue Ridge Parkway">Blue Ridge Parkway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Smoky_Mountains_National_Park" title="Great Smoky Mountains National Park">Great Smoky Mountains National Park</a> are the two most visited national park and unit in the United States with over 25 million visitors in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> The City of <a class="external text" href="http://www.exploreasheville.com/" rel="nofollow">Asheville</a> is consistently voted as one of the top places to visit and live in the United States, known for its rich art deco architecture, mountain scenery and outdoor activities, and liberal and happy residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh</a> many tourists visit the Capital, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=African_American_Cultural_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="African American Cultural Complex (page does not exist)">African American Cultural Complex</a>, <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_Art_Museum_of_Raleigh" title="Contemporary Art Museum of Raleigh">Contemporary Art Museum of Raleigh</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gregg_Museum_of_Art_%26_Design_at_NCSU&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gregg Museum of Art &amp; Design at NCSU (page does not exist)">Gregg Museum of Art &amp; Design at NCSU</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Haywood_Hall_House_%26_Gardens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Haywood Hall House &amp; Gardens (page does not exist)">Haywood Hall House &amp; Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marbles_Kids_Museum" title="Marbles Kids Museum">Marbles Kids Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Museum_of_Art" title="North Carolina Museum of Art">North Carolina Museum of Art</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Museum_of_History" title="North Carolina Museum of History">North Carolina Museum of History</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Museum_of_Natural_Sciences" title="North Carolina Museum of Natural Sciences">North Carolina Museum of Natural Sciences</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Sports_Hall_of_Fame" title="North Carolina Sports Hall of Fame">North Carolina Sports Hall of Fame</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raleigh_City_Museum" title="Raleigh City Museum">Raleigh City Museum</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J._C._Raulston_Arboretum" title="J. C. Raulston Arboretum">J. C. Raulston Arboretum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joel_Lane_House" title="Joel Lane House">Joel Lane House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mordecai_House" title="Mordecai House">Mordecai House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montfort_Hall" title="Montfort Hall">Montfort Hall</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pope_House_Museum" title="Pope House Museum">Pope House Museum</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Hurricanes" title="Carolina Hurricanes">Carolina Hurricanes</a> NHL hockey team is also located in the city.</p>
<p>In the Charlotte area, amenities include the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a> NFL football team and <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Hornets" title="Charlotte Hornets">Charlotte Hornets</a> basketball team, <a href="/wiki/Carowinds" title="Carowinds">Carowinds</a> amusement park, <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Motor_Speedway" title="Charlotte Motor Speedway">Charlotte Motor Speedway</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._National_Whitewater_Center" title="U.S. National Whitewater Center">U.S. National Whitewater Center</a>, and the Discovery Place. Nearby <a href="/wiki/Concord,_North_Carolina" title="Concord, North Carolina">Concord</a> has the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Wolf_Lodge" title="Great Wolf Lodge">Great Wolf Lodge</a> and Sea Life Aquarium.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Conover,_North_Carolina" title="Conover, North Carolina">Conover</a> – <a href="/wiki/Hickory,_North_Carolina" title="Hickory, North Carolina">Hickory</a> area, <a href="/wiki/Hickory_Motor_Speedway" title="Hickory Motor Speedway">Hickory Motor Speedway</a>, RockBarn Golf and Spa, home of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Hickory_Classic_at_Rock_Barn" title="Greater Hickory Classic at Rock Barn">Greater Hickory Classic at Rock Barn</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catawba_County" title="Catawba County">Catawba County</a> Firefighters Museum, and SALT Block attract many tourists to Conover. Hickory which has <a href="/wiki/Valley_Hills_Mall" title="Valley Hills Mall">Valley Hills Mall</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_Triad" title="Piedmont Triad">Piedmont Triad</a>, or center of the state, is home to <a href="/wiki/Krispy_Kreme" title="Krispy Kreme">Krispy Kreme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayberry" title="Mayberry">Mayberry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas_Pete" title="Texas Pete">Texas Pete</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lexington_Barbecue_Festival" title="Lexington Barbecue Festival">Lexington Barbecue Festival</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Moravian_spice_cookies" title="Moravian spice cookies">Moravian cookies</a>. The internationally acclaimed <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Zoo" title="North Carolina Zoo">North Carolina Zoo</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asheboro" title="Asheboro">Asheboro</a> attracts visitors to its animals, plants, and a 57-piece art collection along five miles of shaded pathways in the world's largest-land-area natural-habitat park. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seagrove" title="Seagrove">Seagrove</a>, in the central portion of the state, attracts many tourists along <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pottery_Highway" title="Pottery Highway">Pottery Highway</a> (NC Hwy 705). <a href="/wiki/MerleFest" title="MerleFest">MerleFest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wilkesboro,_North_Carolina" title="Wilkesboro, North Carolina">Wilkesboro</a> attracts more than 80,000 people to its four-day music festival; and Wet 'n Wild Emerald Pointe water park in <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">Greensboro</a> is another attraction.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Outer_Banks" title="Outer Banks">Outer Banks</a> and surrounding beaches attract millions of people to the Atlantic beaches every year.</p>
<p>The mainland northeastern part of the state, having recently adopted the name the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Banks" title="Inner Banks">Inner Banks</a>, is also known as the Albemarle Region, for the <a href="/wiki/Albemarle_Settlements" title="Albemarle Settlements">Albemarle Settlements</a>, some of the first settlements on North Carolina's portion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coastal_Plain" title="Atlantic Coastal Plain">Atlantic Coastal Plain</a>. The regions historic sites are connected by the <a href="/wiki/Historic_Albemarle_Tour" title="Historic Albemarle Tour">Historic Albemarle Tour</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation">Recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">

<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbcaption">
