Cape Hatteras National Seashore near <a href="/wiki/Avon,_North_Carolina" title="Avon, North Carolina">Avon, North Carolina</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>North Carolina provides a large range of recreational activities, from swimming at the beach<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> to <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a> in the mountains. North Carolina offers <a href="/wiki/Autumn_leaf_color" title="Autumn leaf color">fall colors</a>, freshwater and saltwater fishing, hunting, <a href="/wiki/Birdwatching" title="Birdwatching">birdwatching</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agritourism" title="Agritourism">agritourism</a>, <a href="/wiki/All-terrain_vehicle" title="All-terrain vehicle">ATV</a> trails, <a href="/wiki/Hot_air_ballooning" title="Hot air ballooning">ballooning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rock_climbing" title="Rock climbing">rock climbing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biking" title="Biking">biking</a>, hiking, <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boating" title="Boating">boating</a> and sailing, <a href="/wiki/Camping" title="Camping">camping</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canoeing" title="Canoeing">canoeing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caving" title="Caving">caving</a> (spelunking), gardens, and <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">arboretums</a>. North Carolina has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theme_park" title="Theme park">theme parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aquarium" title="Aquarium">aquariums</a>, museums, <a href="/wiki/Historic_site" title="Historic site">historic sites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse" title="Lighthouse">lighthouses</a>, elegant theaters, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concert_hall" title="Concert hall">concert halls</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fine_dining" title="Fine dining">fine dining</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>North Carolinians enjoy outdoor recreation utilizing numerous local bike paths, 34 <a href="/wiki/List_of_North_Carolina_state_parks" title="List of North Carolina state parks">state parks</a>, and 14 <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">national parks</a>. <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> units include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Appalachian_National_Scenic_Trail" title="Appalachian National Scenic Trail">Appalachian National Scenic Trail</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Parkway" title="Blue Ridge Parkway">Blue Ridge Parkway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras_National_Seashore" title="Cape Hatteras National Seashore">Cape Hatteras National Seashore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Lookout_National_Seashore" title="Cape Lookout National Seashore">Cape Lookout National Seashore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sandburg_Home_National_Historic_Site" title="Carl Sandburg Home National Historic Site">Carl Sandburg Home National Historic Site</a> at <a href="/wiki/Flat_Rock,_Henderson_County,_North_Carolina" title="Flat Rock, Henderson County, North Carolina">Flat Rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Raleigh_National_Historic_Site" title="Fort Raleigh National Historic Site">Fort Raleigh National Historic Site</a> at <a href="/wiki/Manteo,_North_Carolina" title="Manteo, North Carolina">Manteo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Smoky_Mountains_National_Park" title="Great Smoky Mountains National Park">Great Smoky Mountains National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guilford_Courthouse_National_Military_Park" title="Guilford Courthouse National Military Park">Guilford Courthouse National Military Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">Greensboro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moores_Creek_National_Battlefield" title="Moores Creek National Battlefield">Moores Creek National Battlefield</a> near <a href="/wiki/Currie,_North_Carolina" title="Currie, North Carolina">Currie</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pender_County,_North_Carolina" title="Pender County, North Carolina">Pender County</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Overmountain_Victory_National_Historic_Trail" title="Overmountain Victory National Historic Trail">Overmountain Victory National Historic Trail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Old_Salem" title="Old Salem">Old Salem National Historic Site</a> in <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem,_North_Carolina" title="Winston-Salem, North Carolina">Winston-Salem</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trail_of_Tears_National_Historic_Trail" title="Trail of Tears National Historic Trail">Trail of Tears National Historic Trail</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wright_Brothers_National_Memorial" title="Wright Brothers National Memorial">Wright Brothers National Memorial</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kill_Devil_Hills,_North_Carolina" title="Kill Devil Hills, North Carolina">Kill Devil Hills</a>. National Forests include <a href="/wiki/Uwharrie_Mountains" title="Uwharrie Mountains">Uwharrie National Forest</a> in central North Carolina, <a href="/wiki/Croatan_National_Forest" title="Croatan National Forest">Croatan National Forest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_North_Carolina" title="Eastern North Carolina">Eastern North Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pisgah_National_Forest" title="Pisgah National Forest">Pisgah National Forest</a> in the northern mountains, and <a href="/wiki/Nantahala_National_Forest" title="Nantahala National Forest">Nantahala National Forest</a> in the southwestern part of the state.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_culture">Arts and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Arts and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_North_Carolina" title="Culture of North Carolina">Culture of North Carolina</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(August 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>North Carolina has rich traditions in art, music, and cuisine. The nonprofit arts and culture industry generates $1.2 billion in direct economic activity in North Carolina, supporting more than 43,600 full-time equivalent jobs and generating $119 million in revenue for local governments and the state of North Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> North Carolina established the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Museum_of_Art" title="North Carolina Museum of Art">North Carolina Museum of Art</a> as the first major museum collection in the country to be formed by state legislation and funding<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> and continues to bring millions into the NC economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Also see this <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_North_Carolina" title="List of museums in North Carolina">list of museums in North Carolina</a>.</p>
<p>One of the more famous arts communities in the state is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seagrove" title="Seagrove">Seagrove</a>, the handmade-pottery capital of the U.S., where artisans create handcrafted pottery inspired by the same traditions that began in this community more than 200 years ago. With nearly 100 shops and galleries scattered throughout the area, visitors can find everything from traditional tableware to folk and collectible art pieces and historical reproductions.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_North_Carolina" title="Music of North Carolina">Music of North Carolina</a></div>
<p>North Carolina boasts a large number of noteworthy <a href="/wiki/List_of_jazz_musicians" title="List of jazz musicians">jazz musicians</a>, some among the most important in the history of the genre. These include: <a href="/wiki/John_Coltrane" title="John Coltrane">John Coltrane</a>, (<a href="/wiki/Hamlet,_North_Carolina" title="Hamlet, North Carolina">Hamlet</a>, <a href="/wiki/High_Point,_North_Carolina" title="High Point, North Carolina">High Point</a>); <a href="/wiki/Thelonious_Monk" title="Thelonious Monk">Thelonious Monk</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mount,_North_Carolina" title="Rocky Mount, North Carolina">Rocky Mount</a>); <a href="/wiki/Billy_Taylor" title="Billy Taylor">Billy Taylor</a> (<a href="/wiki/Greenville,_North_Carolina" title="Greenville, North Carolina">Greenville</a>); <a href="/wiki/Woody_Shaw" title="Woody Shaw">Woody Shaw</a> (<a href="/wiki/Laurinburg,_North_Carolina" title="Laurinburg, North Carolina">Laurinburg</a>); <a href="/wiki/Lou_Donaldson" title="Lou Donaldson">Lou Donaldson</a> (<a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">Durham</a>); <a href="/wiki/Max_Roach" title="Max Roach">Max Roach</a> (<a href="/wiki/Newland,_North_Carolina" title="Newland, North Carolina">Newland</a>); <a href="/wiki/Tal_Farlow" title="Tal Farlow">Tal Farlow</a> (<a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">Greensboro</a>); <a href="/wiki/Albert_Heath" title="Albert Heath">Albert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Heath" title="Jimmy Heath">Jimmy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Percy_Heath" title="Percy Heath">Percy Heath</a> (<a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_North_Carolina" title="Wilmington, North Carolina">Wilmington</a>); <a href="/wiki/Nina_Simone" title="Nina Simone">Nina Simone</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tryon,_North_Carolina" title="Tryon, North Carolina">Tryon</a>); and <a href="/wiki/Billy_Strayhorn" title="Billy Strayhorn">Billy Strayhorn</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hillsborough,_North_Carolina" title="Hillsborough, North Carolina">Hillsborough</a>).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fiddlin%27_Bill_Hensley,_mountain_fiddler,_Asheville,_North_Carolina_(LOC).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="895" data-file-width="1024" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Fiddlin%27_Bill_Hensley%2C_mountain_fiddler%2C_Asheville%2C_North_Carolina_%28LOC%29.jpg/220px-Fiddlin%27_Bill_Hensley%2C_mountain_fiddler%2C_Asheville%2C_North_Carolina_%28LOC%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Fiddlin%27_Bill_Hensley%2C_mountain_fiddler%2C_Asheville%2C_North_Carolina_%28LOC%29.jpg/330px-Fiddlin%27_Bill_Hensley%2C_mountain_fiddler%2C_Asheville%2C_North_Carolina_%28LOC%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Fiddlin%27_Bill_Hensley%2C_mountain_fiddler%2C_Asheville%2C_North_Carolina_%28LOC%29.jpg/440px-Fiddlin%27_Bill_Hensley%2C_mountain_fiddler%2C_Asheville%2C_North_Carolina_%28LOC%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fiddlin%27_Bill_Hensley,_mountain_fiddler,_Asheville,_North_Carolina_(LOC).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fiddlin' Bill Hensley, mountain fiddler, <a href="/wiki/Asheville,_North_Carolina" title="Asheville, North Carolina">Asheville</a>, 1937</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>North Carolina is also famous for its tradition of <a href="/wiki/Old-time_music" title="Old-time music">old-time music</a>, and many recordings were made in the early 20th century by folk-song collector <a href="/wiki/Bascom_Lamar_Lunsford" title="Bascom Lamar Lunsford">Bascom Lamar Lunsford</a>. Musicians such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Ramblers" title="North Carolina Ramblers">North Carolina Ramblers</a> helped solidify the sound of <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country music</a> in the late 1920s, while the influential <a href="/wiki/Bluegrass_music" title="Bluegrass music">bluegrass</a> musician <a href="/wiki/Doc_Watson" title="Doc Watson">Doc Watson</a> also hailed from North Carolina. Both North and South Carolina are hotbeds for traditional rural <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a>, especially the style known as the <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_blues" title="Piedmont blues">Piedmont blues</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ben_Folds_Five" title="Ben Folds Five">Ben Folds Five</a> originated in <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem,_North_Carolina" title="Winston-Salem, North Carolina">Winston-Salem</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Folds" title="Ben Folds">Ben Folds</a> still records and resides in <a href="/wiki/Chapel_Hill,_North_Carolina" title="Chapel Hill, North Carolina">Chapel Hill</a>.</p>
<p>The British band <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a> is named, in part, after Chapel Hill bluesman <a href="/wiki/Floyd_Council" title="Floyd Council">Floyd Council</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Research_Triangle" title="Research Triangle">Research Triangle</a> area has long been a well-known center for <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk</a>, rock, <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">metal</a>, jazz and <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-richie_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-richie-133">[133]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Taylor" title="James Taylor">James Taylor</a> grew up around Chapel Hill, and his 1968 song "<a href="/wiki/Carolina_in_My_Mind" title="Carolina in My Mind">Carolina in My Mind</a>" has been called an unofficial anthem for the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nando100206_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-nando100206-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Other famous musicians from North Carolina include <a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Caesar" title="Shirley Caesar">Shirley Caesar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberta_Flack" title="Roberta Flack">Roberta Flack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clyde_McPhatter" title="Clyde McPhatter">Clyde McPhatter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nnenna_Freelon" title="Nnenna Freelon">Nnenna Freelon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warren_Haynes" title="Warren Haynes">Warren Haynes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Herring" title="Jimmy Herring">Jimmy Herring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Houser" title="Michael Houser">Michael Houser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Church" title="Eric Church">Eric Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Future_Islands" title="Future Islands">Future Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Randy_Travis" title="Randy Travis">Randy Travis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Adams" title="Ryan Adams">Ryan Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Milsap" title="Ronnie Milsap">Ronnie Milsap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Hamilton_(musician)" title="Anthony Hamilton (musician)">Anthony Hamilton</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Avett_Brothers" title="The Avett Brothers">The Avett Brothers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luke_Combs" title="Luke Combs">Luke Combs</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">Metal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk</a> acts such as <a href="/wiki/Corrosion_of_Conformity" title="Corrosion of Conformity">Corrosion of Conformity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Between_the_Buried_and_Me" title="Between the Buried and Me">Between the Buried and Me</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nightmare_Sonata" title="Nightmare Sonata">Nightmare Sonata</a> are native to North Carolina.</p>
<p>EDM producer <a href="/wiki/Porter_Robinson" title="Porter Robinson">Porter Robinson</a> hails from <a href="/wiki/Chapel_Hill,_North_Carolina" title="Chapel Hill, North Carolina">Chapel Hill</a>.</p>
<p>North Carolina is the home of more <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> finalists than any other state: <a href="/wiki/Clay_Aiken" title="Clay Aiken">Clay Aiken</a> (season two), <a href="/wiki/Fantasia_Barrino" title="Fantasia Barrino">Fantasia Barrino</a> (season three), <a href="/wiki/Chris_Daugherty" title="Chris Daugherty">Chris Daugherty</a> (season five), <a href="/wiki/Kellie_Pickler" title="Kellie Pickler">Kellie Pickler</a> (season five), <a href="/wiki/Bucky_Covington" title="Bucky Covington">Bucky Covington</a> (season five), <a href="/wiki/Anoop_Desai" title="Anoop Desai">Anoop Desai</a> (season eight), <a href="/wiki/Scotty_McCreery" title="Scotty McCreery">Scotty McCreery</a> (season ten), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caleb_Johnson_(singer)" title="Caleb Johnson (singer)">Caleb Johnson</a> (season thirteen). North Carolina also has the most <i>American Idol</i> winners with Barrino, McCreery, and Johnson.</p>
<p>In the mountains, the <a href="/wiki/Brevard_Music_Center" title="Brevard Music Center">Brevard Music Center</a> hosts choral, orchestral, and solo performances during its annual summer schedule.</p>
<p>Also, see the <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="North Carolina Music Hall of Fame">North Carolina Music Hall of Fame</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">Shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>North Carolina has a variety of shopping choices. <a href="/wiki/SouthPark_Mall_(Charlotte,_North_Carolina)" title="SouthPark Mall (Charlotte, North Carolina)">SouthPark Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a> is currently the largest in the Carolinas, with almost 2.0 million square feet. Other major malls in Charlotte include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northlake_Mall_(Charlotte)" title="Northlake Mall (Charlotte)">Northlake Mall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Place_Mall" title="Carolina Place Mall">Carolina Place Mall</a> in nearby suburb <a href="/wiki/Pineville,_North_Carolina" title="Pineville, North Carolina">Pineville</a>. Other major malls throughout the state include <a href="/wiki/Hanes_Mall" title="Hanes Mall">Hanes Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem,_North_Carolina" title="Winston-Salem, North Carolina">Winston-Salem</a>; <a href="/wiki/Crabtree_Valley_Mall" title="Crabtree Valley Mall">Crabtree Valley Mall</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Hills_(Raleigh)" title="North Hills (Raleigh)">North Hills Mall</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Triangle_Town_Center" title="Triangle Town Center">Triangle Town Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh</a>; <a href="/wiki/Friendly_Center" title="Friendly Center">Friendly Center</a> and <a href="/wiki/Four_Seasons_Town_Centre" title="Four Seasons Town Centre">Four Seasons Town Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greensboro,_North_Carolina" title="Greensboro, North Carolina">Greensboro</a>; <a href="/wiki/Oak_Hollow_Mall" title="Oak Hollow Mall">Oak Hollow Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/High_Point,_North_Carolina" title="High Point, North Carolina">High Point</a>; <a href="/wiki/Concord_Mills" title="Concord Mills">Concord Mills</a> in <a href="/wiki/Concord,_North_Carolina" title="Concord, North Carolina">Concord</a>; <a href="/wiki/Valley_Hills_Mall" title="Valley Hills Mall">Valley Hills Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hickory,_North_Carolina" title="Hickory, North Carolina">Hickory</a>; <a href="/wiki/Cross_Creek_Mall" title="Cross Creek Mall">Cross Creek Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville,_North_Carolina" title="Fayetteville, North Carolina">Fayetteville</a>; and <a href="/wiki/The_Streets_at_Southpoint" title="The Streets at Southpoint">The Streets at Southpoint</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northgate_Mall_(Durham)" title="Northgate Mall (Durham)">Northgate Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">Durham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independence_Mall_(North_Carolina)" title="Independence Mall (North Carolina)">Independence Mall</a> in Wilmington, North Carolina, and Tanger Outlets in Charlotte, Nags Head, Blowing Rock, and Mebane, North Carolina.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine_and_agriculture">Cuisine and agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Cuisine and agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lexington_Barbecue_Festival_-_Rides.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Lexington_Barbecue_Festival_-_Rides.jpg/220px-Lexington_Barbecue_Festival_-_Rides.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Lexington_Barbecue_Festival_-_Rides.jpg/330px-Lexington_Barbecue_Festival_-_Rides.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Lexington_Barbecue_Festival_-_Rides.jpg/440px-Lexington_Barbecue_Festival_-_Rides.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lexington_Barbecue_Festival_-_Rides.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2008 <a href="/wiki/Lexington_Barbecue_Festival" title="Lexington Barbecue Festival">Lexington Barbecue Festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A culinary staple of North Carolina is pork <a href="/wiki/Barbecue" title="Barbecue">barbecue</a>. There are strong regional differences and rivalries over the sauces and methods used in making the barbecue. The common trend across Western North Carolina is the use of premium grade <a href="/wiki/Boston_butt" title="Boston butt">Boston butt</a>. Western North Carolina pork barbecue uses a tomato-based sauce, and only the pork shoulder (dark meat) is used. Western North Carolina barbecue is commonly referred to as Lexington barbecue after the <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_Triad" title="Piedmont Triad">Piedmont Triad</a> town of <a href="/wiki/Lexington,_North_Carolina" title="Lexington, North Carolina">Lexington</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Lexington_Barbecue_Festival" title="Lexington Barbecue Festival">Lexington Barbecue Festival</a>, which attracts over 100,000 visitors each October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Eastern North Carolina pork barbecue uses a <a href="/wiki/Vinegar" title="Vinegar">vinegar</a>-and-red-pepper-based sauce and the "whole hog" is cooked, thus integrating both white and dark meat.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Krispy_Kreme" title="Krispy Kreme">Krispy Kreme</a>, an international chain of doughnut stores, was started in North Carolina; the company's headquarters are in <a href="/wiki/Winston-Salem,_North_Carolina" title="Winston-Salem, North Carolina">Winston-Salem</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pepsi-Cola" title="Pepsi-Cola">Pepsi-Cola</a> was first produced in 1898 in <a href="/wiki/New_Bern,_North_Carolina" title="New Bern, North Carolina">New Bern</a>. A regional <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drink</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheerwine" title="Cheerwine">Cheerwine</a>, was created and is still based in the city of Salisbury. Despite its name, the hot sauce <a href="/wiki/Texas_Pete" title="Texas Pete">Texas Pete</a> was created in North Carolina; its headquarters are also in Winston-Salem. The <a href="/wiki/Hardee%27s" title="Hardee's">Hardee's</a> fast-food chain was started in <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mount,_North_Carolina" title="Rocky Mount, North Carolina">Rocky Mount</a>. Another fast-food chain, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bojangles%27" title="Bojangles'">Bojangles'</a>, was started in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a>, and has its corporate headquarters there. A popular North Carolina restaurant chain is <a href="/wiki/Golden_Corral" title="Golden Corral">Golden Corral</a>. Started in 1973, the chain was founded in <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville,_North_Carolina" title="Fayetteville, North Carolina">Fayetteville</a>, with headquarters located in <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh</a>. Popular <a href="/wiki/Pickled_cucumber" title="Pickled cucumber">pickle</a> brand <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Olive_Pickle_Company" title="Mount Olive Pickle Company">Mount Olive Pickle Company</a> was founded in <a href="/wiki/Mount_Olive,_North_Carolina" title="Mount Olive, North Carolina">Mount Olive</a> in 1926. Fast casual burger chain <a href="/wiki/Hwy_55_Burgers,_Shakes_%26_Fries" title="Hwy 55 Burgers, Shakes &amp; Fries">Hwy 55 Burgers, Shakes &amp; Fries</a> also makes its home in <a href="/wiki/Mount_Olive,_North_Carolina" title="Mount Olive, North Carolina">Mount Olive</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cook_Out_(restaurant)" title="Cook Out (restaurant)">Cook Out</a>, a popular fast-food chain featuring burgers, hot dogs, and milkshakes in a wide variety of flavors, was founded in Greensboro in 1989 and has begun expanding outside of North Carolina. In 2013, Southern Living named Durham – Chapel Hill the South's "Tastiest City."</p>
<p>Over the last decade, North Carolina has become a cultural epicenter and haven for internationally prize-winning wine (Noni Bacca Winery), internationally prized cheeses (Ashe County), "L'institut International aux Arts Gastronomiques: Conquerront Les Yanks les Truffes, January 15, 2010" international hub for truffles (Garland Truffles), and beer making, as tobacco land has been converted to grape orchards while state laws regulating alcohol content in beer allowed a jump in ABV from 6% to 15%. The Yadkin Valley in particular has become a strengthening market for grape production, while <a href="/wiki/Asheville,_North_Carolina" title="Asheville, North Carolina">Asheville</a> recently won the recognition of being named 'Beer City USA.' <a href="/wiki/Asheville,_North_Carolina" title="Asheville, North Carolina">Asheville</a> boasts the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Carolina_breweries#Breweries" title="North Carolina breweries">breweries</a> per capita of any city in the United States. Recognized and marketed brands of beer in North Carolina include Highland Brewing, Duck Rabbit Brewery, Mother Earth Brewery, Weeping Radish Brewery, Big Boss Brewing, Foothills Brewing, Carolina Brewing Company, Lonerider Brewing, and White Rabbit Brewing Company. North Carolina has large grazing areas for beef and dairy cattle. Truck farms can be found in North Carolina. A truck farm is a small farm where fruits and vegetables are grown to be sold at local markets. The state's shipping, commercial fishing, and lumber industries are important to its economy. Service industries, including education, health care, private research, and retail trade, are also important. Research Triangle Park, a large industrial complex located in the Raleigh-Durham area, is one of the major centers in the country for electronics and medical research</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">Tobacco</a> was one of the first major industries to develop after the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a>. Many farmers grew some tobacco, and the invention of the cigarette made the product especially popular. Winston-Salem is the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/R._J._Reynolds_Tobacco_Company" title="R. J. Reynolds Tobacco Company">R. J. Reynolds Tobacco Company</a> (RJR), founded by <a href="/wiki/R._J._Reynolds" title="R. J. Reynolds">R. J. Reynolds</a> in 1874 as one of 16 tobacco companies in the town. By 1914 it was selling 425 million packs of Camels a year. Today it is the second-largest tobacco company in the U.S. (behind <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Altria_Group" title="Altria Group">Altria Group</a>). RJR is an indirect wholly owned subsidiary of Reynolds American Inc., which in turn is 42% owned by <a href="/wiki/British_American_Tobacco" title="British American Tobacco">British American Tobacco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ships_named_for_the_state">Ships named for the state</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Ships named for the state">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:U.S.S._North_Carolina.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1266" data-file-width="1900" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/U.S.S._North_Carolina.jpg/225px-U.S.S._North_Carolina.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/U.S.S._North_Carolina.jpg/338px-U.S.S._North_Carolina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/U.S.S._North_Carolina.jpg/450px-U.S.S._North_Carolina.jpg 2x" width="225"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U.S.S._North_Carolina.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
USS <i>North Carolina</i> on permanent display in Wilmington</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/USS_North_Carolina" title="USS North Carolina">USS North Carolina</a></div>
<p>Several ships have been named after the state. Most famous is the <a href="/wiki/USS_North_Carolina_(BB-55)" title="USS North Carolina (BB-55)">USS <i>North Carolina</i></a>, a World War II <a href="/wiki/Battleship" title="Battleship">battleship</a>. The ship served in several battles against the forces of Imperial Japan in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean_theater_of_World_War_II" title="Pacific Ocean theater of World War II">Pacific theater</a> during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">war</a>. Now decommissioned, it is part of the USS <i>North Carolina</i> Battleship Memorial in Wilmington. Another <a href="/wiki/USS_North_Carolina_(SSN-777)" title="USS North Carolina (SSN-777)">USS <i>North Carolina</i></a>, a nuclear attack <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarine</a>, was commissioned in Wilmington, North Carolina, on May 3, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_parks">State parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: State parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_North_Carolina_state_parks" title="List of North Carolina state parks">List of North Carolina state parks</a></div>
<p>The state maintains a group of <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">protected areas</a> known as the <b>North Carolina State Park System</b>, which is managed by the North Carolina Division of Parks &amp; Recreation (NCDPR), an agency of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Department_of_Environment_and_Natural_Resources" title="North Carolina Department of Environment and Natural Resources">North Carolina Department of Environment and Natural Resources (NCDENR)</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_symbols">State symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: State symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces_installations">Armed forces installations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Armed forces installations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_News_Photo_110323-A-3108M-004_-_U.S._Army_paratroopers_participate_in_an_advanced_rifle_marksmanship_course_at_Fort_Bragg_N.C._on_March_23_2011._The_paratroopers_are_assigned.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1013" data-file-width="1519" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Defense.gov_News_Photo_110323-A-3108M-004_-_U.S._Army_paratroopers_participate_in_an_advanced_rifle_marksmanship_course_at_Fort_Bragg_N.C._on_March_23_2011._The_paratroopers_are_assigned.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Defense.gov_News_Photo_110323-A-3108M-004_-_U.S._Army_paratroopers_participate_in_an_advanced_rifle_marksmanship_course_at_Fort_Bragg_N.C._on_March_23_2011._The_paratroopers_are_assigned.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Defense.gov_News_Photo_110323-A-3108M-004_-_U.S._Army_paratroopers_participate_in_an_advanced_rifle_marksmanship_course_at_Fort_Bragg_N.C._on_March_23_2011._The_paratroopers_are_assigned.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_News_Photo_110323-A-3108M-004_-_U.S._Army_paratroopers_participate_in_an_advanced_rifle_marksmanship_course_at_Fort_Bragg_N.C._on_March_23_2011._The_paratroopers_are_assigned.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Troopers of the 82nd Airborne Division training on <a href="/wiki/Fort_Bragg" title="Fort Bragg">Fort Bragg</a>, March 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Bragg,_North_Carolina" title="Fort Bragg, North Carolina">Fort Bragg</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville,_North_Carolina" title="Fayetteville, North Carolina">Fayetteville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Pines,_North_Carolina" title="Southern Pines, North Carolina">Southern Pines</a>, is a large and comprehensive military base and is the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/XVIII_Airborne_Corps" title="XVIII Airborne Corps">XVIII Airborne Corps</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._82nd_Airborne_Division" title="U.S. 82nd Airborne Division">82nd Airborne Division</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Army_Special_Operations_Command" title="U.S. Army Special Operations Command">U.S. Army Special Operations Command</a>. Serving as the air wing for Fort Bragg is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pope_Air_Force_Base" title="Pope Air Force Base">Pope Field</a>, also located near Fayetteville.</p>
<p>Located in <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_North_Carolina" title="Jacksonville, North Carolina">Jacksonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Camp_Lejeune" title="Marine Corps Base Camp Lejeune">Marine Corps Base Camp Lejeune</a>, combined with nearby bases <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MCAS_Cherry_Point" title="MCAS Cherry Point">Marine Corps Air Station (MCAS) Cherry Point</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Air_Station_New_River" title="Marine Corps Air Station New River">MCAS New River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camp_Geiger" title="Camp Geiger">Camp Geiger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camp_Gilbert_H._Johnson" title="Camp Gilbert H. Johnson">Camp Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stone_Bay" title="Stone Bay">Stone Bay</a> and Courthouse Bay, makes up the largest concentration of Marines and sailors in the world. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MCAS_Cherry_Point" title="MCAS Cherry Point">MCAS Cherry Point</a> is home of the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Marine_Aircraft_Wing" title="2nd Marine Aircraft Wing">2nd Marine Aircraft Wing</a>. Located in <a href="/wiki/Goldsboro,_North_Carolina" title="Goldsboro, North Carolina">Goldsboro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Johnson_Air_Force_Base" title="Seymour Johnson Air Force Base">Seymour Johnson Air Force Base</a> is home of the <a href="/wiki/4th_Fighter_Wing" title="4th Fighter Wing">4th Fighter Wing</a> and <a href="/wiki/916th_Air_Refueling_Wing" title="916th Air Refueling Wing">916th Air Refueling Wing</a>. One of the busiest air stations in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">United States Coast Guard</a> is located at the <a href="/wiki/Coast_Guard_Air_Station_Elizabeth_City" title="Coast Guard Air Station Elizabeth City">Coast Guard Air Station</a> in <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_City,_North_Carolina" title="Elizabeth City, North Carolina">Elizabeth City</a>. Also stationed in North Carolina is the <a href="/wiki/Military_Ocean_Terminal_Sunny_Point" title="Military Ocean Terminal Sunny Point">Military Ocean Terminal Sunny Point</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southport" title="Southport">Southport</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_sources">Primary sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=North_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Primary sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>Lefler, Hugh (numerous editions since 1934). <i>North Carolina History Told by Contemporaries</i> . <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_Press" title="University of North Carolina Press">University of North Carolina Press</a>.</li>
<li>Jones, H. G. (1984). <i>North Carolina Illustrated, 1524–1984</i>. University of North Carolina Press.</li>
<li><i>North Carolina Manual</i>. Published biennially by the Department of the Secretary of State since 1941.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://library.divinity.duke.edu/ncreligion" rel="nofollow">The Religion in North Carolina Digital Collection</a>. A grant-funded project to provide digital access to publications of and about religious bodies in North Carolina. Partner institutions at <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNC-Chapel_Hill" title="UNC-Chapel Hill">UNC-Chapel Hill</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wake_Forest_University" title="Wake Forest University">Wake Forest University</a> contributed the largest portion of the items in this collection, but the collection is enriched by unique materials from libraries and archives throughout North Carolina. The materials in this collection include local church histories, periodicals, clergy biographies, cookbooks, event programs, directories, and much more.</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>James, Clay; Orr, Douglas, eds. (1971). <i>North Carolina Atlas: Portrait of a Changing Southern State</i>.</li>
<li>Christensen, Rob (2008). <i>The Paradox of Tar Heel Politics</i>. Chapel Hill: <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_Press" title="University of North Carolina Press">University of North Carolina Press</a>.</li>
<li>Cooper, Christopher A.; Knotts, H. Gibbs, eds. (2008). <i>The New Politics of North Carolina</i>. Chapel Hill: University of North Carolina Press.</li>
<li>Crow; Jeffrey J.; Tise, Larry E. (1979). <i>Writing North Carolina History</i>. <a class="external text" href="https://www.questia.com/PM.qst?a=o&amp;d=59237933" rel="nofollow">Online.</a></li>
<li>Eamon, Tom (2014). <i>The Making of a Southern Democracy: North Carolina Politics from Kerr Scott to Pat McCrory.</i> Chapel Hill, North Carolina: University of North Carolina Press.</li>
<li>Fleer, Jack D. (1994). <i>North Carolina Government &amp; Politics</i>. <a class="external text" href="https://www.questia.com/PM.qst?a=o&amp;d=98712979" rel="nofollow">Online political science textbook.</a></li>
<li>Hawks, Francis L. (1857). <i>History of North Carolina, Volumes I and II</i>.</li>
<li>Kersey, Marianne M.; Coble, Ran, eds. (1989). <i>North Carolina Focus: An Anthology on State Government, Politics, and Policy</i>. 2d ed. Raleigh: North Carolina Center for Public Policy Research.</li>
<li>Lefler, Hugh Talmage (1963). <i>A Guide to the Study and Reading of North Carolina History</i>. <a class="external text" href="https://www.questia.com/PM.qst?a=o&amp;d=65419833" rel="nofollow">Online.</a></li>
<li>Lefler, Hugh Talmage; Newsome, Albert Ray (1954, 1963, 1973). <i>North Carolina: The History of a Southern State</i>. Standard textbook.</li>
<li>Link, William A. (2009). <i>North Carolina: Change and Tradition in a Southern State</i>. History by leading scholar.</li>
<li>Luebke, Paul (1990). <i>Tar Heel Politics: Myths and Realities</i>.</li>
<li>Powell, William S. (1979–88). <i>Dictionary of North Carolina Biography</i>. Vol. 1, A-C; vol. 2, D-G; vol. 3, H-K.</li>
<li>Powell, William S. (1958). <i>North Carolina Fiction, 1734–1957: An Annotated Bibliography</i>.</li>
<li>Powell, William S. (1989). <i>North Carolina through Four Centuries</i>. Standard textbook.</li>
<li>Powell, William S.; Mazzocchi, Jay, eds. (2006). <i>Encyclopedia of North Carolina</i>.</li>
<li>Ready, Milton. (2005). <i>The Tar Heel State: A History of North Carolina</i>.</li>
<li>Thuesen, Sarah Caroline. (2013). <i>Greater Than Equal: African American Struggles for Schools and Citizenship in North Carolina, 1919–1965</i>. Chapel Hill, North Carolina: University of North Carolina Press.</li>
<li>WPA Federal Writers' Project (1939). <i>North Carolina: A Guide to the Old North State</i>. Famous <a href="/wiki/Works_Progress_Administration" title="Works Progress Administration">WPA</a> guide to every town.</li>
</ul>
